         </span>
         /
        </a>
       </span>
      </span>
      ) is the most densely populated
      <a href="/wiki/Borough_(New_York_City)" title="Borough (New York City)">
       borough
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
       New York City
      </a>
      , its economic and administrative center, and the city's historical birthplace.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ManhattanRealEstate_3-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ManhattanRealEstate-3">
        [2]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The borough is coterminous with
      <b>
       New York County
      </b>
      , founded on November 1, 1683, as one of the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_New_York" title="List of counties in New York">
       original counties
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">
       U.S. state
      </a>
      of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">
       New York
      </a>
      . The borough consists mostly of
      <b>
       Manhattan Island
      </b>
      , bounded by the
      <a href="/wiki/East_River" title="East River">
       East
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">
       Hudson
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Harlem_River" title="Harlem River">
       Harlem
      </a>
      Rivers, and also includes
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_smaller_islands_in_New_York_City" title="List of smaller islands in New York City">
       several small adjacent islands
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Marble_Hill,_Manhattan" title="Marble Hill, Manhattan">
       Marble Hill
      </a>
      , a small neighborhood on the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._mainland" title="U.S. mainland">
       U.S. mainland
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Manhattan is often described as the cultural and financial capital of the world
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        [3]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        [4]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        [5]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and hosts the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Headquarters" title="United Nations Headquarters">
       United Nations Headquarters
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        [6]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Anchored by
      <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">
       Wall Street
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Financial_District,_Manhattan" title="Financial District, Manhattan">
       Financial District
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan" title="Lower Manhattan">
       Lower Manhattan
      </a>
      , New York City has been called both the most economically powerful city and the leading financial center of the world,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EconomicallyPowerful2015_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-EconomicallyPowerful2015-8">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldEconomicAndFinancialSuperCenter_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WorldEconomicAndFinancialSuperCenter-9">
        [8]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        [9]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        [10]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        [11]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Manhattan is home to the world's two
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_stock_exchanges" title="List of stock exchanges">
       largest stock exchanges
      </a>
      by total
      <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">
       market capitalization
      </a>
      : the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">
       New York Stock Exchange
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/NASDAQ" title="NASDAQ">
       NASDAQ
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYSElargest_13-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYSElargest-13">
        [12]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stockexchangemagnitude_14-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-stockexchangemagnitude-14">
        [13]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many
      <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">
       multinational
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Media_conglomerate" title="Media conglomerate">
       media conglomerates
      </a>
      are based in the borough. It is historically documented to have been purchased by
      <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">
       Dutch
      </a>
      colonists from
      <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">
       Native Americans
      </a>
      in 1626, for 60
      <a href="/wiki/Guilder" title="Guilder">
       guilders
      </a>
      or about $24 in 1626
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        [14]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and US$1051 today.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Netherland_Institute_16-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-New_Netherland_Institute-16">
        [15]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Manhattan real estate has since become among the most expensive in the world, with the value of Manhattan Island, including real estate, estimated to exceed US$3 trillion in 2013;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ManhattanRealEstate_3-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ManhattanRealEstate-3">
        [2]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        [16]
       </a>
      </sup>
      residential property sale prices in Manhattan typically exceeded US$1,400 per square foot ($15,000/m
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      ) as of 2016.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        [17]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      New York County is the
      <a href="/wiki/County_statistics_of_the_United_States#Nationwide_land_area_extremes" title="County statistics of the United States">
       United States' second-smallest county by land area
      </a>
      (larger only than
      <a href="/wiki/Kalawao_County,_Hawaii" title="Kalawao County, Hawaii">
       Kalawao County, Hawaii
      </a>
      ), and is also the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_most_populous_counties_in_the_United_States" title="List of the most populous counties in the United States">
       most densely populated U.S. county
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        [18]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is also one of the most densely populated areas in the world, with a census-estimated 2015 population of 1,644,518
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ManhattanQuickFacts_1-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ManhattanQuickFacts-1">
        [1]
       </a>
      </sup>
      living in a land area of 22.83 square miles (59.13 km
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      ),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        [19]
       </a>
      </sup>
      or 72,033 residents per square mile (27,812/km
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      ),
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population_density#New_York_City_boroughs" title="List of United States cities by population density">
       higher than the density of any individual American city
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        [20]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On business days, the influx of commuters increases that number to over 3.9 million,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        [21]
       </a>
      </sup>
      or more than 170,000 people per square mile (65,600/km
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      ). Manhattan has the third-largest population of New York City's five boroughs, after
      <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">
       Brooklyn
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">
       Queens
      </a>
      , and is the smallest borough in terms of land area.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        [22]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Many districts and landmarks in Manhattan have become well known, as New York City received a record of nearly 60 million tourists in 2015,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYCTouristCount_24-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYCTouristCount-24">
        [23]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Manhattan hosts three of the world's 10 most-visited tourist attractions in 2013:
      <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">
       Times Square
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">
       Central Park
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Grand_Central_Terminal" title="Grand Central Terminal">
       Grand Central Terminal
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ann_Shields_25-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Ann_Shields-25">
        [24]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The borough hosts many world-renowned
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bridges_and_tunnels_in_New_York_City" title="Bridges and tunnels in New York City">
       bridges
      </a>
      , such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Bridge" title="Brooklyn Bridge">
       Brooklyn Bridge
      </a>
      ;
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tallest_buildings_in_New_York_City" title="Tallest buildings in New York City">
       skyscrapers
      </a>
      such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Empire_State_Building" title="Empire State Building">
       Empire State Building
      </a>
      , one of the tallest skyscrapers in the world;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        [25]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_City_parks" title="List of New York City parks">
       parks
      </a>
      , such as Central Park. There are many historically significant places in Manhattan:
      <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Manhattan" title="Chinatown, Manhattan">
       Chinatown
      </a>
      incorporates the highest concentration of Chinese people in the
      <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">
       Western Hemisphere
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        [26]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Stonewall_Inn" title="Stonewall Inn">
       Stonewall Inn
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Village" title="Greenwich Village">
       Greenwich Village
      </a>
      is considered the birthplace of the modern
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gay_rights_movement" title="Gay rights movement">
       gay rights movement
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_28-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-28">
        [27]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        [28]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The City of New York was founded at the southern tip of Manhattan,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ManhattanRealEstate_3-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-ManhattanRealEstate-3">
        [2]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the borough houses
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Hall" title="New York City Hall">
       New York City Hall
      </a>
      , the seat of the
      <a href="/wiki/Government_of_New_York_City" title="Government of New York City">
       City's Government
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        [29]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Numerous colleges and universities are located in Manhattan,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        [30]
       </a>
      </sup>
      including
      <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">
       Columbia University
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">
       New York University
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weill_Cornell_Medical_College" title="Weill Cornell Medical College">
       Weill Cornell Medical College
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_University" title="Rockefeller University">
       Rockefeller University
      </a>
      , which have been ranked among the top 35 in the world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        [31]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        [32]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <table border="1" class="wikitable" style="float:right; text-align:right; font-size:85%; margin:1em;">

        </ul>
       </li>
       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8">
        <a href="#Geography">
         <span class="tocnumber">
          3
         </span>
         <span class="toctext">
          Geography
         </span>
        </a>
        <ul>
         <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9">
          <a href="#Components">
           <span class="tocnumber">

           </span>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
       Etymology
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The name "
      <i>
       Manhattan"
      </i>
      derives from the word
      <i>
       Manna-hata
      </i>
      , as written in the 1609 logbook of Robert Juet, an officer on
      <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson" title="Henry Hudson">
       Henry Hudson
      </a>
      's yacht
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Halve_Maen" title="Halve Maen">
        Halve Maen
       </a>
      </i>
      (
      <i>
       Half Moon
      </i>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        [33]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A 1610 map depicts the name as Manna-hata, twice, on both the west and east sides of the Mauritius River (later named the
      <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">
       Hudson River
      </a>
      ). The word "Manhattan" has been translated as "island of many hills" from the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lenape_language" title="Lenape language">
       Lenape language
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mannahatta_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mannahatta-35">
        [34]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">
       United States Postal Service
      </a>
      prefers that mail addressed to Manhattan use "New York, NY" rather than "Manhattan, NY".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        [35]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">
       Colonial era
       <span id="17th_century">
       </span>
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Colonial era">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peter_Minuit_portrait_New_Amsterdam_1600s_light.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="472" data-file-width="360" height="288" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Peter_Minuit_portrait_New_Amsterdam_1600s_light.jpg/220px-Peter_Minuit_portrait_New_Amsterdam_1600s_light.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Peter_Minuit_portrait_New_Amsterdam_1600s_light.jpg/330px-Peter_Minuit_portrait_New_Amsterdam_1600s_light.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a6/Peter_Minuit_portrait_New_Amsterdam_1600s_light.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Peter_Minuit_portrait_New_Amsterdam_1600s_light.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Peter_Minuit" title="Peter Minuit">
         Peter Minuit
        </a>
        , early 1600s.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CastelloPlanOriginal.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1398" data-file-width="2100" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/CastelloPlanOriginal.jpg/220px-CastelloPlanOriginal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/CastelloPlanOriginal.jpg/330px-CastelloPlanOriginal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/CastelloPlanOriginal.jpg/440px-CastelloPlanOriginal.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CastelloPlanOriginal.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Castello_Plan" title="Castello Plan">
         Castello Plan
        </a>
        showing the Dutch colonial city of
        <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">
         New Amsterdam
        </a>
        in 1660 – then confined to the southern tip of Manhattan Island.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The area that is now Manhattan was long inhabited by the
      <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">
       Lenape
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">
       Native Americans
      </a>
      . In 1524,
      <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">
       Florentine
      </a>
      explorer
      <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_da_Verrazzano" title="Giovanni da Verrazzano">
       Giovanni da Verrazzano
      </a>
      – sailing in service of
      <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_France" title="Francis I of France">
       King Francis I
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
       France
      </a>
      – was the first
      <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">
       European
      </a>
      to visit the area that would become New York City. He entered the
      <a href="/wiki/Strait" title="Strait">
       tidal strait
      </a>
      now known as
      <a href="/wiki/The_Narrows" title="The Narrows">
       The Narrows
      </a>
      aboard his ship
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/La_Dauphine" title="La Dauphine">
        La Dauphine
       </a>
      </i>
      and named the land around
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_New_York_Harbor" title="Upper New York Harbor">
       Upper New York Harbor
      </a>
      <i>
       "
       <a href="/wiki/New_Angoul%C3%AAme" title="New Angoulême">
        New Angoulême
       </a>
       "
      </i>
      , in reference to the family name of King Francis I that was derived from
      <a href="/wiki/Angoul%C3%AAme" title="Angoulême">
       Angoulême
      </a>
      in France; he sailed far enough into the harbor to sight the
      <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">
       Hudson River
      </a>
      , which he referred to in his report to the French king as a "very big river"; and he named the
      <i>
       Bay of Santa Margarita
      </i>
      – what is now Upper New York Bay – after
      <a href="/wiki/Marguerite_de_Navarre" title="Marguerite de Navarre">
       Marguerite de Navarre
      </a>
      , the elder sister of the king.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        [36]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        [37]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      It was not until the voyage of
      <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson" title="Henry Hudson">
       Henry Hudson
      </a>
      , an Englishman who worked for the
      <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">
       Dutch East India Company
      </a>
      , that the area was mapped.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        [38]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Hudson came across Manhattan Island and the native people living there in 1609, and continued up the river that would later bear his name, the
      <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">
       Hudson River
      </a>
      , until he arrived at the site of present day
      <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">
       Albany
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SciAm_40-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SciAm-40">
        [39]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:George_Washington_Statue_at_Federal_Hall.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3450" data-file-width="1896" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/George_Washington_Statue_at_Federal_Hall.JPG/140px-George_Washington_Statue_at_Federal_Hall.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/George_Washington_Statue_at_Federal_Hall.JPG/210px-George_Washington_Statue_at_Federal_Hall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/George_Washington_Statue_at_Federal_Hall.JPG/280px-George_Washington_Statue_at_Federal_Hall.JPG 2x" width="140"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:George_Washington_Statue_at_Federal_Hall.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/John_Quincy_Adams_Ward" title="John Quincy Adams Ward">
         J.Q.A. Ward
        </a>
        's statue of
        <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">
         George Washington
        </a>
        in front of
        <a href="/wiki/Federal_Hall" title="Federal Hall">
         Federal Hall
        </a>
        (on
        <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">
         Wall Street
        </a>
        ) where he was inaugurated as the first
        <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">
         U.S. President
        </a>
        in 1789.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
         <a href="#cite_note-41">
          [40]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      A permanent European presence in
      <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">
       New Netherland
      </a>
      began in 1624 with the founding of a
      <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">
       Dutch
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Fur_trade" title="Fur trade">
       fur trading
      </a>
      settlement on
      <a href="/wiki/Governors_Island" title="Governors Island">
       Governors Island
      </a>
      . In 1625, construction was started on the
      <a href="/wiki/Citadel" title="Citadel">
       citadel
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Fort_Amsterdam" title="Fort Amsterdam">
       Fort Amsterdam
      </a>
      on Manhattan Island, later called
      <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">
       New Amsterdam
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Nieuw Amsterdam
      </i>
      ), in what is now Lower Manhattan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        [41]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tolerance_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Tolerance-43">
        [42]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The 1625 establishment of Fort Amsterdam at the southern tip of Manhattan Island is recognized as the birth of New York City.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        [43]
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to a letter by Pieter Janszoon Schagen,
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Minuit" title="Peter Minuit">
       Peter Minuit
      </a>
      and Dutch colonists acquired Manhattan on May 24, 1626, from unnamed Native American people, which are believed to have been
      <a href="/wiki/Metoac" title="Metoac">
       Canarsee Indians
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">
       Lenape
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        [44]
       </a>
      </sup>
      in exchange for trade goods worth 60
      <a href="/wiki/Guilder" title="Guilder">
       guilders
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Netherland_Institute_16-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-New_Netherland_Institute-16">
        [15]
       </a>
      </sup>
      often said to be worth US$24, although accounting for
      <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">
       inflation
      </a>
      , it actually amounts to around US$1,050 in 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        [45]
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to the writer Nathaniel Benchley, Minuit conducted the transaction with Seyseys, chief of the Canarsees, who were only too happy to accept valuable merchandise in exchange for the island that was actually mostly controlled by the
      <a href="/wiki/Wappinger" title="Wappinger">
       Weckquaesgeeks
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        [46]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1647,
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Stuyvesant" title="Peter Stuyvesant">
       Peter Stuyvesant
      </a>
      was appointed as the last Dutch Director General of the colony.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        [47]
       </a>
      </sup>
      New Amsterdam was formally incorporated as a city on February 2, 1653.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        [48]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1664, the English conquered
      <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">
       New Netherland
      </a>
      and renamed it "New York" after the English
      <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">
       Duke of York and Albany
      </a>
      , the future King James II.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        [49]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Dutch, under Director General Stuyvesant, successfully negotiated with the English to produce 24 articles of provisional transfer, which sought to retain for the extant citizens of New Netherland their previously attained liberties (including
      <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">
       freedom of religion
      </a>
      ) under new colonial English rulers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        [50]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        [51]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Dutch Republic regained it in August 1673 with a fleet of 21 ships, renaming the city "New Orange". New Netherland was ceded permanently to the English in November 1674 through the Treaty of Westminster,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        [52]
       </a>
      </sup>
      in exchange for
      <a href="/wiki/Run_(island)" title="Run (island)">
       Run Island
      </a>
      which was the long-coveted last link in the Dutch
      <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">
       nutmeg
      </a>
      trading monopoly in
      <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
       Indonesia
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        [53]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="American_Revolution_and_the_early_United_States">
       American Revolution and the early United States
       <span id="18th_century">
       </span>
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: American Revolution and the early United States">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Manhattan was at the heart of the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_and_New_Jersey_campaign" title="New York and New Jersey campaign">
       New York Campaign
      </a>
      , a series of major battles in the early
      <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">
       American Revolutionary War
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">
       Continental Army
      </a>
      was forced to abandon Manhattan after the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Washington" title="Battle of Fort Washington">
       Battle of Fort Washington
      </a>
      on November 16, 1776. The city, greatly damaged by the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Fire_of_New_York_(1776)" title="Great Fire of New York (1776)">
       Great Fire of New York
      </a>
      during the campaign, became the British political and military center of operations in North America for the remainder of the war.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        [54]
       </a>
      </sup>
      British occupation lasted until November 25, 1783, when
      <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">
       George Washington
      </a>
      returned to Manhattan, as
      <a href="/wiki/Evacuation_Day_(New_York)" title="Evacuation Day (New York)">
       the last British forces left the city
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        [55]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      From January 11, 1785, to the fall of 1788, New York City was the fifth of five
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_capitals_in_the_United_States" title="List of capitals in the United States">
       capitals of the United States
      </a>
      under the
      <a href="/wiki/Articles_of_Confederation" title="Articles of Confederation">
       Articles of Confederation
      </a>
      , with the
      <a href="/wiki/Continental_Congress" title="Continental Congress">
       Continental Congress
      </a>
      meeting at
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Hall" title="New York City Hall">
       New York City Hall
      </a>
      (then at
      <a href="/wiki/Fraunces_Tavern" title="Fraunces Tavern">
       Fraunces Tavern
      </a>
      ). New York was the first capital under the newly enacted
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">
       Constitution of the United States
      </a>
      , from March 4, 1789, to August 12, 1790, at
      <a href="/wiki/Federal_Hall" title="Federal Hall">
       Federal Hall
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        [56]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Federal Hall was also the site of where the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court" title="United States Supreme Court">
       United States Supreme Court
      </a>
      met for the first time,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        [57]
       </a>
      </sup>
      the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Bill_of_Rights" title="United States Bill of Rights">
       United States Bill of Rights
      </a>
      were drafted and ratified,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cwf_59-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cwf-59">
        [58]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and where the
      <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Ordinance" title="Northwest Ordinance">
       Northwest Ordinance
      </a>
      was adopted, establishing measures for adding new states to the
      <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">
       Union
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        [59]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">
       19th century
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 19th century">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:George_Schlegel_-_George_Degen_-_New_York_1873.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7128" data-file-width="9768" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/George_Schlegel_-_George_Degen_-_New_York_1873.jpg/220px-George_Schlegel_-_George_Degen_-_New_York_1873.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/George_Schlegel_-_George_Degen_-_New_York_1873.jpg/330px-George_Schlegel_-_George_Degen_-_New_York_1873.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/George_Schlegel_-_George_Degen_-_New_York_1873.jpg/440px-George_Schlegel_-_George_Degen_-_New_York_1873.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:George_Schlegel_-_George_Degen_-_New_York_1873.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Manhattan in 1873. The
        <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Bridge" title="Brooklyn Bridge">
         Brooklyn Bridge
        </a>
        was under construction from 1870 until 1883.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      New York grew as an economic center, first as a result of
      <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton" title="Alexander Hamilton">
       Alexander Hamilton
      </a>
      's policies and practices as the first
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_the_Treasury" title="Secretary of the Treasury">
       Secretary of the Treasury
      </a>
      and, later, with the opening of the
      <a href="/wiki/Erie_Canal" title="Erie Canal">
       Erie Canal
      </a>
      in 1825, which connected the Atlantic port to the vast agricultural markets of the
      <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">
       Midwestern United States
      </a>
      and Canada.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        [60]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lankevich-p67_62-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-lankevich-p67-62">
        [61]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By 1810 New York City, then confined to Manhattan, had surpassed
      <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">
       Philadelphia
      </a>
      as the largest city in the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        [62]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Tammany_Hall" title="Tammany Hall">
       Tammany Hall
      </a>
      , a
      <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">
       Democratic Party
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Political_machine" title="Political machine">
       political machine
      </a>
      , began to grow in influence with the support of many of the
      <a href="/wiki/Irish_diaspora" title="Irish diaspora">
       immigrant Irish
      </a>
      , culminating in the election of the first Tammany mayor,
      <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Wood" title="Fernando Wood">
       Fernando Wood
      </a>
      , in 1854. Tammany Hall dominated local politics for decades.
      <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">
       Central Park
      </a>
      , which opened to the public in 1858, became the first landscaped public park in an American city.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        [b]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      New York City played a complex role in the
      <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">
       American Civil War
      </a>
      . The city's strong commercial ties to the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_South" title="American South">
       American South
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        [64]
       </a>
      </sup>
      its growing immigrant population (prior to then largely from Germany and Ireland; beginning in the late 1850s waves of Italian; and Central, and Eastern European Jews began flowing in en-masse), anger about
      <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">
       conscription
      </a>
      sizzled and resentment at those who could afford to pay $300 to avoid service, led to resentment against Lincoln's war policies, plus the racial element, fomented paranoia about free Blacks taking the poor immigrants' jobs,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        [65]
       </a>
      </sup>
      culminated in the three-day-long
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Draft_Riots" title="New York Draft Riots">
       New York Draft Riots
      </a>
      of July 1863. These intense war-time riots are counted among the worst incidents of
      <a href="/wiki/Civil_disorder" title="Civil disorder">
       civil disorder
      </a>
      in American history, with an estimated 119 participants and passersby massacred.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        [66]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The rate of immigration from Europe grew steeply after the Civil War, and New York became the first stop for millions seeking a new life in the United States, a role acknowledged by the dedication of the
      <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Liberty" title="Statue of Liberty">
       Statue of Liberty
      </a>
      on October 28, 1886, a gift from the people of France.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        [67]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        [68]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The new European immigration brought further social upheaval. In a city of tenements packed with poorly paid laborers from dozens of nations, the city was a hotbed of
      <a href="/wiki/Revolution" title="Revolution">
       revolution
      </a>
      (including
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anarchist" title="Anarchist">
       anarchists
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist" title="Communist">
       communists
      </a>
      among others),
      <a href="/wiki/Syndicalism" title="Syndicalism">
       syndicalism
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Racketeering" title="Racketeering">
       racketeering
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unionization" title="Unionization">
       unionization
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1883, the opening of the
      <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Bridge" title="Brooklyn Bridge">
       Brooklyn Bridge
      </a>
      established a road connection to
      <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">
       Brooklyn
      </a>
      , across the
      <a href="/wiki/East_River" title="East River">
       East River
      </a>
      . In 1874, the western portion of the present
      <a href="/wiki/The_Bronx" title="The Bronx">
       Bronx County
      </a>
      was transferred to New York County from
      <a href="/wiki/Westchester_County,_New_York" title="Westchester County, New York">
       Westchester County
      </a>
      , and in 1895 the remainder of the present Bronx County was annexed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        [69]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1898, when New York City consolidated with three neighboring counties to form "the
      <a href="/wiki/City_of_Greater_New_York" title="City of Greater New York">
       City of Greater New York
      </a>
      ", Manhattan and the Bronx, though still one county, were established as two separate
      <a href="/wiki/Borough_(New_York_City)" title="Borough (New York City)">
       boroughs
      </a>
      . On January 1, 1914, the New York state legislature created Bronx County, and New York County was reduced to its present boundaries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        [70]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="center">
      <div class="thumb tnone">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:752px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Viele_Map_1865.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3115" data-file-width="9859" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Viele_Map_1865.jpg/750px-Viele_Map_1865.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Viele_Map_1865.jpg/1125px-Viele_Map_1865.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Viele_Map_1865.jpg/1500px-Viele_Map_1865.jpg 2x" width="750"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Viele_Map_1865.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The "Sanitary &amp; Topographical Map of the City and Island of New York", commonly known as the Viele Map, was created by
         <a href="/wiki/Egbert_Ludovicus_Viele" title="Egbert Ludovicus Viele">
          Egbert Ludovicus Viele
         </a>
         in 1865
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">
       20th century
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 20th century">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mulberry_Street_NYC_c1900_LOC_3g04637u_edit.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2067" data-file-width="2800" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Mulberry_Street_NYC_c1900_LOC_3g04637u_edit.jpg/220px-Mulberry_Street_NYC_c1900_LOC_3g04637u_edit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Mulberry_Street_NYC_c1900_LOC_3g04637u_edit.jpg/330px-Mulberry_Street_NYC_c1900_LOC_3g04637u_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Mulberry_Street_NYC_c1900_LOC_3g04637u_edit.jpg/440px-Mulberry_Street_NYC_c1900_LOC_3g04637u_edit.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mulberry_Street_NYC_c1900_LOC_3g04637u_edit.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Manhattan's
        <a href="/wiki/Little_Italy,_Manhattan" title="Little Italy, Manhattan">
         Little Italy
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Lower_East_Side" title="Lower East Side">
         Lower East Side
        </a>
        , circa 1900
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The construction of the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">
       New York City Subway
      </a>
      , which opened in 1904, helped bind the new city together, as did additional bridges to Brooklyn. In the 1920s, Manhattan experienced large arrivals of African-Americans as part of the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Migration_(African_American)" title="Great Migration (African American)">
       Great Migration
      </a>
      from the southern United States, and the
      <a href="/wiki/Harlem_Renaissance" title="Harlem Renaissance">
       Harlem Renaissance
      </a>
      , part of a larger boom time in the
      <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_in_the_United_States" title="Prohibition in the United States">
       Prohibition
      </a>
      era that included new
      <a href="/wiki/Skyscraper" title="Skyscraper">
       skyscrapers
      </a>
      competing for the skyline. New York City became the most populous city in the world in 1925, overtaking London, which had reigned for a century.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        [71]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Manhattan's majority
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">
       white
      </a>
      ethnic group declined from 98.7% in 1900 to 58.3% by 1990.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        [72]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On March 25, 1911, the
      <a href="/wiki/Triangle_Shirtwaist_Factory_fire" title="Triangle Shirtwaist Factory fire">
       Triangle Shirtwaist Factory fire
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Village" title="Greenwich Village">
       Greenwich Village
      </a>
      killed 146 garment workers. The disaster eventually led to overhauls of the city's fire department, building codes, and workplace regulations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        [73]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The period between the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_War" title="World War">
       World Wars
      </a>
      saw the election of reformist mayor
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fiorello_La_Guardia" title="Fiorello La Guardia">
       Fiorello La Guardia
      </a>
      and the fall of
      <a href="/wiki/Tammany_Hall" title="Tammany Hall">
       Tammany Hall
      </a>
      after 80 years of political dominance.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        [74]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As the city's demographics stabilized, labor unionization brought new protections and affluence to the working class, the city's government and infrastructure underwent a dramatic overhaul under La Guardia. Despite the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">
       Great Depression
      </a>
      , some of the world's tallest skyscrapers were completed in Manhattan during the 1930s, including numerous
      <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">
       Art Deco
      </a>
      masterpieces that are still part of the city's skyline today, most notably the
      <a href="/wiki/Empire_State_Building" title="Empire State Building">
       Empire State Building
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Chrysler_Building" title="Chrysler Building">
       Chrysler Building
      </a>
      , and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GE_Building" title="GE Building">
       GE Building
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kissing_the_War_Goodbye.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1271" data-file-width="1204" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Kissing_the_War_Goodbye.jpg/170px-Kissing_the_War_Goodbye.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Kissing_the_War_Goodbye.jpg/255px-Kissing_the_War_Goodbye.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Kissing_the_War_Goodbye.jpg/340px-Kissing_the_War_Goodbye.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kissing_the_War_Goodbye.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Victory_over_Japan_Day" title="Victory over Japan Day">
          Victory over Japan Day
         </a>
        </i>
        in Times Square, 1945
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Returning World War II veterans created a postwar economic boom, which led to the development of huge housing developments targeted at returning veterans, the largest being
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_Cooper_Village%E2%80%94Stuyvesant_Town" title="Peter Cooper Village—Stuyvesant Town">
       Peter Cooper Village-Stuyvesant Town
      </a>
      , which opened in 1947.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        [75]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1952, the UN relocated from its first headquarters near
      <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">
       Queens
      </a>
      , to the East Side of Manhattan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Akenuwa2015_78-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Akenuwa2015-78">
        [76]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Stonewall_riots" title="Stonewall riots">
       Stonewall riots
      </a>
      were a series of spontaneous, violent demonstrations by members of the
      <a href="/wiki/LGBT_community" title="LGBT community">
       gay community
      </a>
      against a
      <a href="/wiki/Police_raid" title="Police raid">
       police raid
      </a>
      that took place in the early morning hours of June 28, 1969, at the
      <a href="/wiki/Stonewall_Inn" title="Stonewall Inn">
       Stonewall Inn
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Village" title="Greenwich Village">
       Greenwich Village
      </a>
      neighborhood of Lower Manhattan. They are widely considered to constitute the single most important event leading to the
      <a href="/wiki/Gay_liberation" title="Gay liberation">
       gay liberation
      </a>
      movement and the modern fight for
      <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_United_States" title="LGBT rights in the United States">
       LGBT rights in the United States
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-diversity_79-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-diversity-79">
        [77]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        [78]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the 1970s, job losses due to
      <a href="/wiki/Deindustrialization" title="Deindustrialization">
       industrial restructuring
      </a>
      caused New York City, including Manhattan, to suffer from economic problems and rising crime rates.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        [79]
       </a>
      </sup>
      While a resurgence in the financial industry greatly improved the city's economic health in the 1980s, New York's crime rate continued to increase through the decade and into the beginning of the 1990s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        [80]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The 1980s saw a rebirth of
      <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">
       Wall Street
      </a>
      , and Manhattan reclaimed its role at the center of the worldwide
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Financial_industry" title="Financial industry">
       financial industry
      </a>
      . The 1980s also saw Manhattan at the heart of the AIDS crisis, with Greenwich Village at its epicenter. The organizations
      <a href="/wiki/Gay_Men%27s_Health_Crisis" title="Gay Men's Health Crisis">
       Gay Men's Health Crisis
      </a>
      (GMHC) and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS_Coalition_to_Unleash_Power" title="AIDS Coalition to Unleash Power">
       AIDS Coalition to Unleash Power
      </a>
      (ACT UP) were founded to advocate on behalf of those stricken with the disease.
     </p>
     <p>
      By the 1990s, crime rates started to drop dramatically due to revised police strategies, improving economic opportunities,
      <a href="/wiki/Gentrification" title="Gentrification">
       gentrification
      </a>
      , and new residents, both American transplants and new immigrants from Asia and Latin America. Murder rates that had reached 2,245 in 1990 plummeted to 537 by 2008, and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crack_epidemic_(United_States)" title="Crack epidemic (United States)">
       crack epidemic
      </a>
      and its associated drug-related violence came under greater control.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        [81]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The outflow of population turned around, as the city once again became the destination of immigrants from around the world, joining with low interest rates and Wall Street bonuses to fuel the growth of the real estate market.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        [82]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Important new sectors, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Alley" title="Silicon Alley">
       Silicon Alley
      </a>
      , emerged in Manhattan's economy.
     </p>
     <table style="background:transparent;margin-top:0.5em;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto">
      <tr>
       <td>

            </div>
           </div>
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr style="vertical-align:top">

            <a href="/wiki/Chrysler_Building" title="Chrysler Building">

           </div>

            .

            on September 11, 2001.
           </div>
          </td>
