     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
       Economy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Economy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Photos_NewYork1_032.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Photos_NewYork1_032.jpg/220px-Photos_NewYork1_032.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Photos_NewYork1_032.jpg/330px-Photos_NewYork1_032.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Photos_NewYork1_032.jpg/440px-Photos_NewYork1_032.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Photos_NewYork1_032.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">
         New York Stock Exchange
        </a>
        on
        <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">
         Wall Street
        </a>
        , the
        <a href="/wiki/List_of_stock_exchanges#Major_stock_exchanges" title="List of stock exchanges">
         world's largest stock exchange
        </a>
        by total
        <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">
         market capitalization
        </a>
        of its listed companies.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stockexchangemagnitude_14-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-stockexchangemagnitude-14">
          [13]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_New_York_City" title="Economy of New York City">
       Economy of New York City
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Manhattan is the economic engine of New York City, with its 2.3 million workers in 2007 drawn from the entire
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area" title="New York metropolitan area">
       New York metropolitan area
      </a>
      accounting for almost two-thirds of all jobs in New York City.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">
       <a href="#cite_note-181">
        [177]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the first quarter of 2014, the average weekly wage in Manhattan (New York County) was $2,749, representing the highest total among large counties in the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">
       <a href="#cite_note-182">
        [178]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Manhattan's workforce is overwhelmingly focused on
      <a href="/wiki/White-collar_worker" title="White-collar worker">
       white collar
      </a>
      professions, with manufacturing nearly extinct. Manhattan also has the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_counties_by_per_capita_income" title="United States counties by per capita income">
       highest per capita income of any county in the United States
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2010, Manhattan's daytime population was swelling to 3.94 million, with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commuter" title="Commuter">
       commuters
      </a>
      adding a net 1.48 million people to the population, along with visitors, tourists, and commuting students. The commuter influx of 1.61 million workers coming into Manhattan was the largest of any county or city in the country,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183">
       <a href="#cite_note-183">
        [179]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and was more than triple the 480,000 commuters who headed into second-ranked Washington, D.C.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184">
       <a href="#cite_note-184">
        [180]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_sector">
       Financial sector
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Financial sector">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">
       Wall Street
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Manhattan's most important economic sector lies in its role as the headquarters for the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Financial_center" title="Financial center">
       U.S. financial industry
      </a>
      , metonymously known as Wall Street. The borough's
      <a href="/wiki/Security_(finance)" title="Security (finance)">
       securities
      </a>
      industry, enumerating 163,400 jobs in August 2013, continues to form the largest segment of the city's financial sector and an important economic engine for Manhattan, accounting in 2012 for 5 percent of private sector jobs in New York City, 8.5 percent (US$3.8 billion) of the city's tax revenue, and 22 percent of the city's total wages, including an average salary of US$360,700.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185">
       <a href="#cite_note-185">
        [181]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Wall Street
      <a href="/wiki/Investment_banking" title="Investment banking">
       investment banking
      </a>
      fees in 2012 totaled approximately US$40 billion,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186">
       <a href="#cite_note-186">
        [182]
       </a>
      </sup>
      while in 2013, senior New York City bank officers who manage
      <a href="/wiki/Risk_management" title="Risk management">
       risk and compliance
      </a>
      functions earned as much as US$324,000 annually.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187">
       <a href="#cite_note-187">
        [183]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lower_Manhattan_viewed_from_Brooklyn.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Lower_Manhattan_viewed_from_Brooklyn.jpg/300px-Lower_Manhattan_viewed_from_Brooklyn.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Lower_Manhattan_viewed_from_Brooklyn.jpg/450px-Lower_Manhattan_viewed_from_Brooklyn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Lower_Manhattan_viewed_from_Brooklyn.jpg/600px-Lower_Manhattan_viewed_from_Brooklyn.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lower_Manhattan_viewed_from_Brooklyn.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Financial_District,_Manhattan" title="Financial District, Manhattan">
         Financial District
        </a>
        of
        <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan" title="Lower Manhattan">
         Lower Manhattan
        </a>
        , viewed from
        <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">
         Brooklyn
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Lower Manhattan is home to the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">
       New York Stock Exchange
      </a>
      (NYSE), on Wall Street, and the
      <a href="/wiki/NASDAQ" title="NASDAQ">
       NASDAQ
      </a>
      , at
      <a href="/wiki/One_Liberty_Plaza" title="One Liberty Plaza">
       165 Broadway
      </a>
      , representing the world's largest and second largest
      <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">
       stock exchanges
      </a>
      , respectively, when measured both by overall share trading value and by total
      <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">
       market capitalization
      </a>
      of their listed companies in 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stockexchangemagnitude_14-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-stockexchangemagnitude-14">
        [13]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/NYSE_MKT" title="NYSE MKT">
       NYSE MKT
      </a>
      (formerly the American Stock Exchange, AMEX),
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Board_of_Trade" title="New York Board of Trade">
       New York Board of Trade
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mercantile_Exchange" title="New York Mercantile Exchange">
       New York Mercantile Exchange
      </a>
      (NYMEX) are also located downtown. In July 2013,
      <a href="/wiki/NYSE_Euronext" title="NYSE Euronext">
       NYSE Euronext
      </a>
      , the operator of the New York Stock Exchange, took over the administration of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_interbank_offered_rate" title="London interbank offered rate">
       London interbank offered rate
      </a>
      from the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Bankers_Association" title="British Bankers Association">
       British Bankers Association
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">
       <a href="#cite_note-188">
        [184]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_sector">
       Corporate sector
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Corporate sector">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      New York City is home to the most corporate headquarters of any city in the nation, the overwhelming majority based in Manhattan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189">
       <a href="#cite_note-189">
        [185]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Manhattan contained over 500 million square feet (46.5 million m
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      ) of office space in 2015,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ManhattanOfficeSpace_190-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ManhattanOfficeSpace-190">
        [186]
       </a>
      </sup>
      making it the largest office market in the United States,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">
       <a href="#cite_note-191">
        [187]
       </a>
      </sup>
      while
      <a href="/wiki/Midtown_Manhattan" title="Midtown Manhattan">
       Midtown Manhattan
      </a>
      , with nearly 400 million square feet (37.2 million m
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      ) in 2015,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ManhattanOfficeSpace_190-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ManhattanOfficeSpace-190">
        [186]
       </a>
      </sup>
      is the largest
      <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">
       central business district
      </a>
      in the world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192">
       <a href="#cite_note-192">
        [188]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of 2013
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , the global
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_advertising_agencies" title="List of advertising agencies">
       advertising agencies
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Omnicom_Group" title="Omnicom Group">
       Omnicom Group
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interpublic_Group" title="Interpublic Group">
       Interpublic Group
      </a>
      , both based in Manhattan, had combined annual revenues of approximately US$21 billion, reflecting New York City's role as the top global center for the
      <a href="/wiki/Advertising" title="Advertising">
       advertising industry
      </a>
      , which is metonymously referred to as
      <a href="/wiki/Madison_Avenue#Advertising_industry" title="Madison Avenue">
       "Madison Avenue"
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Technology_sectors">
       Technology sectors
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Technology sectors">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Alley" title="Silicon Alley">
       Silicon Alley
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Further information:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tech_companies_in_Manhattan" title="Tech companies in Manhattan">
       Tech companies in Manhattan
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Silicon Alley, centered in Manhattan, has evolved into a
      <a href="/wiki/Metonymy" title="Metonymy">
       metonym
      </a>
      for the sphere encompassing the New York City metropolitan region's
      <a href="/wiki/High_tech" title="High tech">
       high tech
      </a>
      industries
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193">
       <a href="#cite_note-193">
        [189]
       </a>
      </sup>
      including, the
      <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">
       Internet
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/New_media" title="New media">
       new media
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telecommunications" title="Telecommunications">
       telecommunications
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Digital_media" title="Digital media">
       digital media
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Software_development" title="Software development">
       software development
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">
       biotechnology
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Game_design" title="Game design">
       game design
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Financial_technology" title="Financial technology">
       financial technology
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       fintech
      </i>
      ), and other fields within
      <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">
       information technology
      </a>
      that are supported by the area's
      <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship_ecosystem" title="Entrepreneurship ecosystem">
       entrepreneurship ecosystem
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Venture_capital" title="Venture capital">
       venture capital
      </a>
      investments. As of 2014
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , New York City hosted 300,000 employees in the tech sector.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194">
       <a href="#cite_note-194">
        [190]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNMoney_195-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CNNMoney-195">
        [191]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2015, Silicon Alley generated over US$7.3 billion in venture capital investment,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VentureCapitalNY1_196-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-VentureCapitalNY1-196">
        [192]
       </a>
      </sup>
      most based in Manhattan, as well as in
      <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">
       Brooklyn
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">
       Queens
      </a>
      , and elsewhere in the region. High technology
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Startup_companies" title="Startup companies">
       startup companies
      </a>
      and employment are growing in Manhattan and across New York City, bolstered by the city's emergence as a global node of
      <a href="/wiki/Innovation" title="Innovation">
       creativity
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship" title="Entrepreneurship">
       entrepreneurship
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VentureCapitalNY1_196-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-VentureCapitalNY1-196">
        [192]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_tolerance" title="Social tolerance">
       social tolerance
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SocialToleranceNY1_197-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SocialToleranceNY1-197">
        [193]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">
       environmental sustainability
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EnvironmentalSustainabilityNY1_198-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-EnvironmentalSustainabilityNY1-198">
        [194]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EnvironmentalSustainabilityNY2_199-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-EnvironmentalSustainabilityNY2-199">
        [195]
       </a>
      </sup>
      as well as New York's position as the leading Internet hub and telecommunications center in North America, including its vicinity to several
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transatlantic_telephone_cable" title="Transatlantic telephone cable">
       transatlantic fiber optic trunk lines
      </a>
      , the city's
      <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_capital" title="Intellectual capital">
       intellectual capital
      </a>
      , and its extensive outdoor
      <a href="/wiki/Wireless_network" title="Wireless network">
       wireless connectivity
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200">
       <a href="#cite_note-200">
        [196]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Communications" title="Verizon Communications">
       Verizon Communications
      </a>
      , headquartered at 140
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Street_(Manhattan)" title="West Street (Manhattan)">
       West Street
      </a>
      in Lower Manhattan, was at the final stages in 2014 of completing a US$3 billion
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fiberoptic_communication" title="Fiberoptic communication">
       fiberoptic telecommunications
      </a>
      upgrade throughout New York City.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201">
       <a href="#cite_note-201">
        [197]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of October 2014, New York City hosted 300,000 employees in the tech sector,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNMoney_195-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-CNNMoney-195">
        [191]
       </a>
      </sup>
      with a significant proportion in Manhattan.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">
       biotechnology
      </a>
      sector is also growing in Manhattan based upon the city's strength in academic scientific
      <a href="/wiki/Research" title="Research">
       research
      </a>
      and public and commercial financial support. By mid-2014, Accelerator, a biotech
      <a href="/wiki/Investment" title="Investment">
       investment
      </a>
      firm, had raised more than US$30 million from
      <a href="/wiki/Investor" title="Investor">
       investors
      </a>
      , including
      <a href="/wiki/Eli_Lilly_and_Company" title="Eli Lilly and Company">
       Eli Lilly and Company
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Pfizer" title="Pfizer">
       Pfizer
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Johnson_%26_Johnson" title="Johnson &amp; Johnson">
       Johnson &amp; Johnson
      </a>
      , for initial funding to create biotechnology startups at the Alexandria Center for Life Science, which encompasses more than 700,000 square feet (65,000 m
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      ) on
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/29th_Street_(Manhattan)" title="29th Street (Manhattan)">
       East 29th Street
      </a>
      and promotes collaboration among scientists and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Entrepreneur" title="Entrepreneur">
       entrepreneurs
      </a>
      at the center and with nearby academic, medical, and research institutions. The
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Economic_Development_Corporation" title="New York City Economic Development Corporation">
       New York City Economic Development Corporation
      </a>
      's Early Stage Life Sciences Funding Initiative and venture capital partners, including
      <a href="/wiki/Celgene" title="Celgene">
       Celgene
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">
       General Electric
      </a>
      Ventures, and Eli Lilly, committed a minimum of US$100 million to help launch 15 to 20 ventures in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_sciences" title="Life sciences">
       life sciences
      </a>
      and biotechnology.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202">
       <a href="#cite_note-202">
        [198]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2011, Mayor
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_R._Bloomberg" title="Michael R. Bloomberg">
       Michael R. Bloomberg
      </a>
      had announced his choice of
      <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">
       Cornell University
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technion-Israel_Institute_of_Technology" title="Technion-Israel Institute of Technology">
       Technion-Israel Institute of Technology
      </a>
      to build a US$2 billion graduate school of
      <a href="/wiki/Applied_science" title="Applied science">
       applied sciences
      </a>
      on
      <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Island" title="Roosevelt Island">
       Roosevelt Island
      </a>
      , Manhattan, with the goal of transforming New York City into the world's premier technology capital.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203">
       <a href="#cite_note-203">
        [199]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204">
       <a href="#cite_note-204">
        [200]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1_times_square_night_2013.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4912" data-file-width="7360" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/1_times_square_night_2013.jpg/250px-1_times_square_night_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/1_times_square_night_2013.jpg/375px-1_times_square_night_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/1_times_square_night_2013.jpg/500px-1_times_square_night_2013.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1_times_square_night_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">
         Times Square
        </a>
        is the hub of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadway_theater" title="Broadway theater">
         Broadway theater
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Theater_District,_Manhattan" title="Theater District, Manhattan">
         district
        </a>
        and a major cultural venue in Manhattan. It also has one of the highest annual attendance rates of any tourist attraction in the world, estimated at 50 million.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ann_Shields_25-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ann_Shields-25">
          [24]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">
       Tourism
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Tourism">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_New_York_City" title="Tourism in New York City">
       Tourism in New York City
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Tourism is vital to Manhattan's economy, and the landmarks of Manhattan are the focus of New York City's tourists, enumerating nearly 60 million visitors in 2015.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYCTouristCount_24-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYCTouristCount-24">
        [23]
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to
      <a href="/wiki/The_Broadway_League" title="The Broadway League">
       The Broadway League
      </a>
      , shows on
      <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">
       Broadway
      </a>
      sold approximately US$1.27 billion worth of tickets in the 2013–2014 season, an increase of 11.4% from US$1.139 billion in the 2012–2013 season; attendance in 2013–2014 stood at 12.21 million, representing a 5.5% increase from the 2012–2013 season's 11.57 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-league_205-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-league-205">
        [201]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Manhattan was on track to have an estimated 90,000
      <a href="/wiki/Hotel" title="Hotel">
       hotel
      </a>
      rooms at the end of 2014, a 10% increase from 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206">
       <a href="#cite_note-206">
        [202]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Real_estate">
       Real estate
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Real estate">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Real estate is a major force in Manhattan's economy, and indeed the city's, as the total value of all New York City property was assessed at US$914.8 billion for the 2015
      <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year" title="Fiscal year">
       fiscal year
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYC_real_estate_207-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYC_real_estate-207">
        [203]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Manhattan has perennially been home to some of the nation's, as well as the world's, most valuable real estate, including the
      <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner_Center" title="Time Warner Center">
       Time Warner Center
      </a>
      , which had the highest-listed market value in the city in 2006 at US$1.1 billion,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208">
       <a href="#cite_note-208">
        [204]
       </a>
      </sup>
      to be subsequently surpassed in October 2014 by the
      <a href="/wiki/Waldorf_Astoria_New_York" title="Waldorf Astoria New York">
       Waldorf Astoria New York
      </a>
      , which became the most expensive hotel ever sold after being purchased by the Anbang Insurance Group, based in China, for
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$1.95 billion
      </span>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robert_Frank_209-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Robert_Frank-209">
        [205]
       </a>
      </sup>
      When 450 Park Avenue was sold on July 2, 2007, for US$510 million, about US$1,589 per square foot (US$17,104/m²), it broke the barely month-old record for an American office building of US$1,476 per square foot (US$15,887/m²) based on the sale of 660
      <a href="/wiki/Madison_Avenue" title="Madison Avenue">
       Madison Avenue
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210">
       <a href="#cite_note-210">
        [206]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2014, Manhattan was home to six of the top ten
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zip_code" title="Zip code">
       zip codes
      </a>
      in the United States by median housing price.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211">
       <a href="#cite_note-211">
        [207]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Manhattan had approximately 520 million square feet (48.1 million m²) of office space in 2013,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212">
       <a href="#cite_note-212">
        [208]
       </a>
      </sup>
      making it the largest office market in the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213">
       <a href="#cite_note-213">
        [209]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Midtown Manhattan is the largest
      <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">
       central business district
      </a>
      in the nation based on office space,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214">
       <a href="#cite_note-214">
        [210]
       </a>
      </sup>
      while Lower Manhattan is the third-largest (after
      <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
       Chicago
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Loop" title="Chicago Loop">
       Loop
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215">
       <a href="#cite_note-215">
        [211]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216">
       <a href="#cite_note-216">
        [212]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
       Media
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Media">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Media_in_New_York_City" title="Media in New York City">
       Media in New York City
      </a>
     </div>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="News">
       News
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: News">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Manhattan is served by the major New York City dailies, including
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">
        The New York Times
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_Daily_News" title="New York Daily News">
        New York Daily News
       </a>
      </i>
      , and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_Post" title="New York Post">
        New York Post
       </a>
      </i>
      , which are all headquartered in the borough. The nation's largest newspaper by circulation,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">
        The Wall Street Journal
       </a>
      </i>
      , is also based there. Other daily newspapers include
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/AM_New_York" title="AM New York">
        AM New York
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Villager_(Manhattan)" title="The Villager (Manhattan)">
        The Villager
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_New_York_Amsterdam_News" title="The New York Amsterdam News">
        The New York Amsterdam News
       </a>
      </i>
      , based in Harlem, is one of the leading African American weekly newspapers in the United States.
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">
        The Village Voice
       </a>
      </i>
      is a leading alternative weekly based in the borough.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217">
       <a href="#cite_note-217">
        [213]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Television.2C_radio.2C_film">
       Television, radio, film
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Television, radio, film">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_set_in_New_York_City" title="List of films set in New York City">
       List of films set in New York City
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_television_shows_set_in_New_York_City" title="List of television shows set in New York City">
       List of television shows set in New York City
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The television industry developed in New York and is a significant employer in the city's economy. The four major American broadcast networks,
      <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">
       ABC
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">
       NBC
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">
       CBS
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">
       Fox
      </a>
      , as well as
      <a href="/wiki/Univision" title="Univision">
       Univision
      </a>
      , are all headquartered in Manhattan, as are many cable channels, including
      <a href="/wiki/MSNBC" title="MSNBC">
       MSNBC
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">
       MTV
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Fox_News" title="Fox News">
       Fox News
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">
       HBO
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central" title="Comedy Central">
       Comedy Central
      </a>
      . In 1971,
      <a href="/wiki/WLIB" title="WLIB">
       WLIB
      </a>
      became New York's first black-owned radio station and the crown jewel of
      <a href="/wiki/Inner_City_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Inner City Broadcasting Corporation">
       Inner City Broadcasting Corporation
      </a>
      . A co-founder of Inner City was
      <a href="/wiki/Percy_Sutton" title="Percy Sutton">
       Percy Sutton
      </a>
      , a former Manhattan borough president and long one of the city's most powerful black leaders.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218">
       <a href="#cite_note-218">
        [214]
       </a>
      </sup>
      WLIB began broadcasts for the African-American community in 1949 and regularly interviewed civil rights leaders like
      <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_X" title="Malcolm X">
       Malcolm X
      </a>
      and aired live broadcasts from conferences of the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Association_for_the_Advancement_of_Colored_People" title="National Association for the Advancement of Colored People">
       NAACP
      </a>
      . Influential
      <a href="/wiki/WQHT" title="WQHT">
       WQHT
      </a>
      , also known as
      <i>
       Hot 97
      </i>
      , claims to be the premier hip-hop station in the United States.
      <a href="/wiki/WNYC" title="WNYC">
       WNYC
      </a>
      , comprising an AM and FM signal, has the largest public radio audience in the nation and is the most-listened to commercial or non-commercial radio station in Manhattan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219">
       <a href="#cite_note-219">
        [215]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/WBAI" title="WBAI">
       WBAI
      </a>
      , with news and information programming, is one of the few socialist radio stations operating in the United States.
     </p>
     <p>
      The oldest
      <a href="/wiki/Public-access_television" title="Public-access television">
       public-access television
      </a>
      cable TV channel in the United States is the
      <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Neighborhood_Network" title="Manhattan Neighborhood Network">
       Manhattan Neighborhood Network
      </a>
      , founded in 1971, offers eclectic local programming that ranges from a jazz hour to discussion of labor issues to foreign language and religious programming.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220">
       <a href="#cite_note-220">
        [216]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/NY1" title="NY1">
       NY1
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner_Cable" title="Time Warner Cable">
       Time Warner Cable
      </a>
      's local news channel, is known for its beat coverage of City Hall and state politics.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_scholarly_activity">
       Education and scholarly activity
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Education and scholarly activity">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:492px;max-width:492px">
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:244px;max-width:244px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Butler_Library_-_1000px_-_AC.jpg">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="664" data-file-width="1000" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Butler_Library_-_1000px_-_AC.jpg/242px-Butler_Library_-_1000px_-_AC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Butler_Library_-_1000px_-_AC.jpg/363px-Butler_Library_-_1000px_-_AC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Butler_Library_-_1000px_-_AC.jpg/484px-Butler_Library_-_1000px_-_AC.jpg 2x" width="242"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         <a href="/wiki/Butler_Library" title="Butler Library">
          Butler Library
         </a>
         at
         <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">
          Columbia University
         </a>
         , described as one of the most beautiful college libraries in the United States
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221">
          <a href="#cite_note-221">
           [217]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:244px;max-width:244px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stuyvesant_HS.jpg">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Stuyvesant_HS.jpg/242px-Stuyvesant_HS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Stuyvesant_HS.jpg/363px-Stuyvesant_HS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Stuyvesant_HS.jpg/484px-Stuyvesant_HS.jpg 2x" width="242"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         <a href="/wiki/Stuyvesant_High_School" title="Stuyvesant High School">
          Stuyvesant High School
         </a>
         , highly regarded as one of the best public high schools in the country
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222">
          <a href="#cite_note-222">
           [218]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div style="clear:left">
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Education_in_New_York_City" title="Education in New York City">
       Education in New York City
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_high_schools_in_New_York_City" title="List of high schools in New York City">
       List of high schools in New York City
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_New_York_City" title="List of colleges and universities in New York City">
       List of colleges and universities in New York City
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Education in Manhattan is provided by a vast number of public and private institutions. Public schools in the borough are operated by the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Department_of_Education" title="New York City Department of Education">
       New York City Department of Education
      </a>
      , the largest public school system in the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223">
       <a href="#cite_note-223">
        [219]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Charter_school" title="Charter school">
       Charter schools
      </a>
      include
      <a href="/wiki/Success_Academy_Charter_Schools" title="Success Academy Charter Schools">
       Success Academy Harlem 1 through 5, Success Academy Upper West
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Public_Prep" title="Public Prep">
       Public Prep
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Some of the best-known New York City public high schools, such as
      <a href="/wiki/The_Beacon_School" title="The Beacon School">
       Beacon High School
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Stuyvesant_High_School" title="Stuyvesant High School">
       Stuyvesant High School
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fiorello_H._LaGuardia_High_School_of_Music_%26_Art_and_Performing_Arts" title="Fiorello H. LaGuardia High School of Music &amp; Art and Performing Arts">
       Fiorello H. LaGuardia High School
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/High_School_of_Fashion_Industries" title="High School of Fashion Industries">
       High School of Fashion Industries
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt_High_School_(New_York_City,_New_York)" title="Eleanor Roosevelt High School (New York City, New York)">
       Eleanor Roosevelt High School
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NYC_Lab_School" title="NYC Lab School">
       NYC Lab School
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Center_for_Science_and_Mathematics" title="Manhattan Center for Science and Mathematics">
       Manhattan Center for Science and Mathematics
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hunter_College_High_School" title="Hunter College High School">
       Hunter College High School
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/High_School_for_Math,_Science_and_Engineering_at_City_College" title="High School for Math, Science and Engineering at City College">
       High School for Math, Science and Engineering at City College
      </a>
      are located in Manhattan.
      <a href="/wiki/Bard_High_School_Early_College" title="Bard High School Early College">
       Bard High School Early College
      </a>
      , a hybrid school created by
      <a href="/wiki/Bard_College" title="Bard College">
       Bard College
      </a>
      , serves students from around the city.
     </p>
     <p>
      Many prestigious private prep schools are located in Manhattan, including the
      <a href="/wiki/Upper_East_Side" title="Upper East Side">
       Upper East Side
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Brearley_School" title="Brearley School">
       Brearley School
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Dalton_School" title="Dalton School">
       Dalton School
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Browning_School" title="Browning School">
       Browning School
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Spence_School" title="Spence School">
       Spence School
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chapin_School_(Manhattan)" title="Chapin School (Manhattan)">
       Chapin School
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Nightingale-Bamford_School" title="Nightingale-Bamford School">
       Nightingale-Bamford School
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Convent_of_the_Sacred_Heart_(New_York)" title="Convent of the Sacred Heart (New York)">
       Convent of the Sacred Heart
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hewitt_School" title="Hewitt School">
       Hewitt School
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Saint_David%27s_School_(New_York_City)" title="Saint David's School (New York City)">
       Saint David's School
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Loyola_School_(New_York_City)" title="Loyola School (New York City)">
       Loyola School
      </a>
      , along with the
      <a href="/wiki/Upper_West_Side" title="Upper West Side">
       Upper West Side
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_School_(New_York_City)" title="Collegiate School (New York City)">
       Collegiate School
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Trinity_School_(New_York_City)" title="Trinity School (New York City)">
       Trinity School
      </a>
      . The prestigious
      <a href="/wiki/Regis_High_School_(New_York_City)" title="Regis High School (New York City)">
       Regis High School
      </a>
      , on the
      <a href="/wiki/Upper_East_Side" title="Upper East Side">
       Upper East Side
      </a>
      , is the only all-scholarship Catholic high school for boys in the country. The borough is also home to two private schools that are known as the most diverse in the nation,
      <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Country_School" title="Manhattan Country School">
       Manhattan Country School
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_International_School" title="United Nations International School">
       United Nations International School
      </a>
      . Manhattan has the only official Italian American school in the U.S., La Scuola d'Italia.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224">
       <a href="#cite_note-224">
        [220]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NYU%27s_Bobst_library-2.jpg">

       </a>

         Elmer Holmes Bobst Library
        </a>
        at
        <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">
         New York University
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_York_Public_Library_May_2011.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/New_York_Public_Library_May_2011.JPG/220px-New_York_Public_Library_May_2011.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/New_York_Public_Library_May_2011.JPG/330px-New_York_Public_Library_May_2011.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/New_York_Public_Library_May_2011.JPG/440px-New_York_Public_Library_May_2011.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_York_Public_Library_May_2011.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/New_York_Public_Library_Main_Branch" title="New York Public Library Main Branch">
         New York Public Library Main Branch
        </a>
        at 42nd St. and Fifth Ave.; built (1897–1911) and replaced the
        <a href="/wiki/Croton_Distributing_Reservoir" title="Croton Distributing Reservoir">
         Croton Reservoir
        </a>
        ;
        <a href="/wiki/Carr%C3%A8re_and_Hastings" title="Carrère and Hastings">
         Carrère and Hastings
        </a>
        , architects.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      As of 2003
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , 52.3% of Manhattan residents over age 25 have a
      <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor's degree">
       bachelor's degree
      </a>
      , the fifth highest of all counties in the country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225">
       <a href="#cite_note-225">
        [221]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By 2005, about 60% of residents were college graduates and some 25% had earned advanced degrees, giving Manhattan one of the nation's densest concentrations of highly educated people.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226">
       <a href="#cite_note-226">
        [222]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Manhattan has various colleges and universities, including
      <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">
       Columbia University
      </a>
      (and its affiliate
      <a href="/wiki/Barnard_College" title="Barnard College">
       Barnard College
      </a>
      ),
      <a href="/wiki/Cooper_Union" title="Cooper Union">
       Cooper Union
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Marymount_Manhattan_College" title="Marymount Manhattan College">
       Marymount Manhattan College
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Institute_of_Technology" title="New York Institute of Technology">
       New York Institute of Technology
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">
       New York University
      </a>
      (NYU),
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Juilliard_School" title="The Juilliard School">
       The Juilliard School
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Pace_University" title="Pace University">
       Pace University
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Berkeley_College" title="Berkeley College">
       Berkeley College
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/The_New_School" title="The New School">
       The New School
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Yeshiva_University" title="Yeshiva University">
       Yeshiva University
      </a>
      , and a campus of
      <a href="/wiki/Fordham_University" title="Fordham University">
       Fordham University
      </a>
      . Other schools include
      <a href="/wiki/Bank_Street_College_of_Education" title="Bank Street College of Education">
       Bank Street College of Education
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Boricua_College" title="Boricua College">
       Boricua College
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Theological_Seminary_of_America" title="Jewish Theological Seminary of America">
       Jewish Theological Seminary of America
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_School_of_Music" title="Manhattan School of Music">
       Manhattan School of Music
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_College_of_New_York" title="Metropolitan College of New York">
       Metropolitan College of New York
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/School_of_Visual_Arts" title="School of Visual Arts">
       School of Visual Arts
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Touro_College" title="Touro College">
       Touro College
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Theological_Seminary_in_the_City_of_New_York" title="Union Theological Seminary in the City of New York">
       Union Theological Seminary
      </a>
      . Several other private institutions maintain a Manhattan presence, among them
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._John%27s_University_(Jamaica,_New_York)" title="St. John's University (Jamaica, New York)">
       St. John's University
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_College_of_New_Rochelle" title="The College of New Rochelle">
       The College of New Rochelle
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Pratt_Institute" title="Pratt Institute">
       Pratt Institute
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/City_University_of_New_York" title="City University of New York">
       City University of New York
      </a>
      (CUNY), the municipal college system of New York City, is the largest urban university system in the United States, serving more than 226,000 degree students and a roughly equal number of adult, continuing and professional education students.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227">
       <a href="#cite_note-227">
        [223]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A third of college graduates in New York City graduate from CUNY, with the institution enrolling about half of all college students in New York City. CUNY senior colleges located in Manhattan include:
      <a href="/wiki/Baruch_College" title="Baruch College">
       Baruch College
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/City_College_of_New_York" title="City College of New York">
       City College of New York
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hunter_College" title="Hunter College">
       Hunter College
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/John_Jay_College_of_Criminal_Justice" title="John Jay College of Criminal Justice">
       John Jay College of Criminal Justice
      </a>
      , and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CUNY_Graduate_Center" title="CUNY Graduate Center">
       CUNY Graduate Center
      </a>
      (graduate studies and doctoral granting institution). The only CUNY community college located in Manhattan is the
      <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Manhattan_Community_College" title="Borough of Manhattan Community College">
       Borough of Manhattan Community College
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York" title="State University of New York">
       State University of New York
      </a>
      is represented by the
      <a href="/wiki/Fashion_Institute_of_Technology" title="Fashion Institute of Technology">
       Fashion Institute of Technology
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_State_College_of_Optometry" title="State University of New York State College of Optometry">
       State University of New York State College of Optometry
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Stony_Brook_Manhattan" title="Stony Brook Manhattan">
       Stony Brook University – Manhattan
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Manhattan is a world center for training and education in medicine and the life sciences.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228">
       <a href="#cite_note-228">
        [224]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The city as a whole receives the second-highest amount of annual funding from the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">
       National Institutes of Health
      </a>
      among all U.S. cities,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229">
       <a href="#cite_note-229">
        [225]
       </a>
      </sup>
      the bulk of which goes to Manhattan's research institutions, including
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memorial_Sloan-Kettering_Cancer_Center" title="Memorial Sloan-Kettering Cancer Center">
       Memorial Sloan-Kettering Cancer Center
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_University" title="Rockefeller University">
       Rockefeller University
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Sinai_School_of_Medicine" title="Mount Sinai School of Medicine">
       Mount Sinai School of Medicine
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University_College_of_Physicians_and_Surgeons" title="Columbia University College of Physicians and Surgeons">
       Columbia University College of Physicians and Surgeons
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weill_Cornell_Medical_College" title="Weill Cornell Medical College">
       Weill Cornell Medical College
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_University_School_of_Medicine" title="New York University School of Medicine">
       New York University School of Medicine
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Manhattan is served by the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Public_Library" title="New York Public Library">
       New York Public Library
      </a>
      , which has the largest collection of any public library system in the country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230">
       <a href="#cite_note-230">
        [226]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The five units of the Central Library—Mid-Manhattan Library, Donnell Library Center, The
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Public_Library_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="New York Public Library for the Performing Arts">
       New York Public Library for the Performing Arts
      </a>
      , Andrew Heiskell Braille and Talking Book Library and the Science, Industry and Business Library—are all located in Manhattan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231">
       <a href="#cite_note-231">
        [227]
       </a>
      </sup>
      More than 35 other branch libraries are located in the borough.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232">
       <a href="#cite_note-232">
        [228]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_contemporary_life">
       Culture and contemporary life
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Culture and contemporary life">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_New_York_City" title="Culture of New York City">
       Culture of New York City
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Music_of_New_York_City" title="Music of New York City">
       Music of New York City
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guggenheim_museum_exterior.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="582" data-file-width="790" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Guggenheim_museum_exterior.jpg/225px-Guggenheim_museum_exterior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Guggenheim_museum_exterior.jpg/338px-Guggenheim_museum_exterior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Guggenheim_museum_exterior.jpg/450px-Guggenheim_museum_exterior.jpg 2x" width="225"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Guggenheim_museum_exterior.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Frank Lloyd Wright's
        <a href="/wiki/Solomon_R._Guggenheim_Museum" title="Solomon R. Guggenheim Museum">
         Solomon R. Guggenheim Museum
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Image-Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_entrance_NYC_NY.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1548" data-file-width="1907" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Image-Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_entrance_NYC_NY.JPG/225px-Image-Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_entrance_NYC_NY.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Image-Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_entrance_NYC_NY.JPG/338px-Image-Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_entrance_NYC_NY.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Image-Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_entrance_NYC_NY.JPG/450px-Image-Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_entrance_NYC_NY.JPG 2x" width="225"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Image-Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art_entrance_NYC_NY.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art" title="Metropolitan Museum of Art">
         Metropolitan Museum of Art
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Manhattan has been the scene of many important American cultural movements. In 1912, about 20,000 workers, a quarter of them women, marched upon
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_Square_Park" title="Washington Square Park">
       Washington Square Park
      </a>
      to commemorate the
      <a href="/wiki/Triangle_Shirtwaist_Factory_fire" title="Triangle Shirtwaist Factory fire">
       Triangle Shirtwaist Factory fire
      </a>
      , which killed 146 workers on March 25, 1911. Many of the women wore fitted tucked-front blouses like those manufactured by the Triangle Shirtwaist Company, a clothing style that became the working woman's uniform and a symbol of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Women%27s_liberation" title="Women's liberation">
       women's liberation
      </a>
      , reflecting the alliance of labor and suffrage movements.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233">
       <a href="#cite_note-233">
        [229]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Harlem_Renaissance" title="Harlem Renaissance">
       Harlem Renaissance
      </a>
      in the 1920s established the African-American literary canon in the United States and introduced writers
      <a href="/wiki/Langston_Hughes" title="Langston Hughes">
       Langston Hughes
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Zora_Neale_Hurston" title="Zora Neale Hurston">
       Zora Neale Hurston
      </a>
      . Manhattan's vibrant visual art scene in the 1950s and 1960s was a center of the American
      <a href="/wiki/Pop_art" title="Pop art">
       pop art
      </a>
      movement, which gave birth to such giants as
      <a href="/wiki/Jasper_Johns" title="Jasper Johns">
       Jasper Johns
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Roy_Lichtenstein" title="Roy Lichtenstein">
       Roy Lichtenstein
      </a>
      . Perhaps no other artist is as associated with the downtown pop art movement of the late 1970s as
      <a href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol" title="Andy Warhol">
       Andy Warhol
      </a>
      , who socialized at clubs like
      <a href="/wiki/Serendipity_3" title="Serendipity 3">
       Serendipity 3
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Studio_54" title="Studio 54">
       Studio 54
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lincoln_Center_Twilight.jpg">
        <img alt="The corner of a lit up plaza with a fountain in the center and the ends of two brightly lit buildings with tall arches on the square." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1501" data-file-width="2000" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Lincoln_Center_Twilight.jpg/225px-Lincoln_Center_Twilight.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Lincoln_Center_Twilight.jpg/338px-Lincoln_Center_Twilight.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Lincoln_Center_Twilight.jpg/450px-Lincoln_Center_Twilight.jpg 2x" width="225"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lincoln_Center_Twilight.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Lincoln Center for the Performing Arts">
         Lincoln Center for the Performing Arts
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Broadway theatre is often considered the highest professional form of theatre in the United States. Plays and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Musical_theater" title="Musical theater">
       musicals
      </a>
      are staged in one of the 39 larger professional theatres with at least 500 seats, almost all in and around Times Square.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234">
       <a href="#cite_note-234">
        [230]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Off-Broadway" title="Off-Broadway">
       Off-Broadway
      </a>
      theatres feature productions in venues with 100–500 seats.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235">
       <a href="#cite_note-235">
        [231]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Lincoln Center for the Performing Arts">
       Lincoln Center for the Performing Arts
      </a>
      , anchoring
      <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Square,_Manhattan" title="Lincoln Square, Manhattan">
       Lincoln Square
      </a>
      on the Upper West Side of Manhattan, is home to 12 influential arts organizations, including the
      <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Opera" title="Metropolitan Opera">
       Metropolitan Opera
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Opera" title="New York City Opera">
       New York City Opera
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Philharmonic" title="New York Philharmonic">
       New York Philharmonic
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Ballet" title="New York City Ballet">
       New York City Ballet
      </a>
      , as well as the
      <a href="/wiki/Vivian_Beaumont_Theater" title="Vivian Beaumont Theater">
       Vivian Beaumont Theater
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Juilliard_School" title="Juilliard School">
       Juilliard School
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jazz_at_Lincoln_Center" title="Jazz at Lincoln Center">
       Jazz at Lincoln Center
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Alice_Tully_Hall" title="Alice Tully Hall">
       Alice Tully Hall
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Manhattan is also home to some of the most extensive art collections in the world, both contemporary and historical, including the
      <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art" title="Metropolitan Museum of Art">
       Metropolitan Museum of Art
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Modern_Art" title="Museum of Modern Art">
       Museum of Modern Art
      </a>
      (MoMA), the
      <a href="/wiki/Frick_Collection" title="Frick Collection">
       Frick Collection
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Museum_of_American_Art" title="Whitney Museum of American Art">
       Whitney Museum of American Art
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lloyd_Wright" title="Frank Lloyd Wright">
       Frank Lloyd Wright
      </a>
      -designed
      <a href="/wiki/Solomon_R._Guggenheim_Museum" title="Solomon R. Guggenheim Museum">
       Guggenheim Museum
      </a>
      . The Upper East Side has many art galleries,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236">
       <a href="#cite_note-236">
        [232]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237">
       <a href="#cite_note-237">
        [233]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the downtown neighborhood of
      <a href="/wiki/Chelsea,_Manhattan" title="Chelsea, Manhattan">
       Chelsea
      </a>
      is known for its more than 200 art galleries that are home to modern art from both upcoming and established artists.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238">
       <a href="#cite_note-238">
        [234]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239">
       <a href="#cite_note-239">
        [235]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Manhattan is the borough most closely associated with New York City by non-residents; even some natives of New York City's boroughs outside Manhattan will describe a trip to Manhattan as "going to the city".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240">
       <a href="#cite_note-240">
        [236]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The borough has a place in several American
      <a href="/wiki/Idiom" title="Idiom">
       idioms
      </a>
      . The phrase
      <i>
       a New York minute
      </i>
      is meant to convey a very short time, sometimes in hyperbolic form, as in "perhaps faster than you would believe is possible". It refers to the rapid pace of life in Manhattan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241">
       <a href="#cite_note-241">
        [237]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The term "
      <a href="/wiki/Melting_pot" title="Melting pot">
       melting pot
      </a>
      " was first popularly coined to describe the densely populated immigrant neighborhoods on the
      <a href="/wiki/Lower_East_Side" title="Lower East Side">
       Lower East Side
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Israel_Zangwill" title="Israel Zangwill">
       Israel Zangwill
      </a>
      's play
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Melting_Pot_(play)" title="The Melting Pot (play)">
        The Melting Pot
       </a>
      </i>
      , which was an adaptation of
      <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">
       William Shakespeare
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Romeo_and_Juliet" title="Romeo and Juliet">
        Romeo and Juliet
       </a>
      </i>
      set by Zangwill in New York City in 1908.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242">
       <a href="#cite_note-242">
        [238]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The iconic
      <a href="/wiki/Flatiron_Building" title="Flatiron Building">
       Flatiron Building
      </a>
      is said to have been the source of the phrase "
      <a href="/wiki/23_skidoo_(phrase)" title="23 skidoo (phrase)">
       23 skidoo
      </a>
      " or scram, from what cops would shout at men who tried to get glimpses of women's dresses being blown up by the winds created by the triangular building.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243">
       <a href="#cite_note-243">
        [239]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The "
      <a href="/wiki/Big_Apple" title="Big Apple">
       Big Apple
      </a>
      " dates back to the 1920s, when a reporter heard the term used by New Orleans stablehands to refer to New York City's racetracks and named his racing column "Around The Big Apple."
      <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">
       Jazz
      </a>
      musicians adopted the term to refer to the city as the world's jazz capital, and a 1970s ad campaign by the New York Convention and Visitors Bureau helped popularize the term.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244">
       <a href="#cite_note-244">
        [240]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
       Sports
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>

        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Msg2005d.JPG">

       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Msg2005d.JPG" title="Enlarge">
