        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">
         Madison Square Garden
        </a>
        is home to the
        <a href="/wiki/New_York_Rangers" title="New York Rangers">
         Rangers
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/New_York_Knicks" title="New York Knicks">
         Knicks
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/New_York_Liberty" title="New York Liberty">
         Liberty
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NSAPINY9_EXTR.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="956" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/NSAPINY9_EXTR.jpg/220px-NSAPINY9_EXTR.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/NSAPINY9_EXTR.jpg/330px-NSAPINY9_EXTR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/NSAPINY9_EXTR.jpg/440px-NSAPINY9_EXTR.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NSAPINY9_EXTR.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The Skating Pond in
        <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">
         Central Park
        </a>
        , 1862
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Manhattan is home to the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">
       NBA
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Knicks" title="New York Knicks">
       New York Knicks
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">
       NHL
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Rangers" title="New York Rangers">
       New York Rangers
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_National_Basketball_Association" title="Women's National Basketball Association">
       WNBA
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Liberty" title="New York Liberty">
       New York Liberty
      </a>
      , who all play their home games at
      <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">
       Madison Square Garden
      </a>
      , the only major professional sports arena in the borough. The
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">
       New York Jets
      </a>
      proposed a
      <a href="/wiki/West_Side_Stadium" title="West Side Stadium">
       West Side Stadium
      </a>
      for their home field, but the proposal was eventually defeated in June 2005, leaving them at
      <a href="/wiki/MetLife_Stadium" title="MetLife Stadium">
       MetLife Stadium
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/East_Rutherford,_New_Jersey" title="East Rutherford, New Jersey">
       East Rutherford, New Jersey
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Today, Manhattan is the only borough in New York City that does not have a
      <a href="/wiki/Professional_baseball" title="Professional baseball">
       professional baseball
      </a>
      franchise.
      <a href="/wiki/The_Bronx" title="The Bronx">
       The Bronx
      </a>
      has the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">
       Yankees
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">
       American League
      </a>
      ) and
      <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">
       Queens
      </a>
      has the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">
       Mets
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">
       National League
      </a>
      ) of
      <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">
       Major League Baseball
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">
       Minor League Baseball
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Cyclones" title="Brooklyn Cyclones">
       Brooklyn Cyclones
      </a>
      play in
      <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">
       Brooklyn
      </a>
      , while the
      <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island_Yankees" title="Staten Island Yankees">
       Staten Island Yankees
      </a>
      play in
      <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island" title="Staten Island">
       Staten Island
      </a>
      . Yet three of the four major league teams to play in New York City played in Manhattan. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Giants_(NL)" title="New York Giants (NL)">
       New York Giants
      </a>
      played in the various incarnations of the
      <a href="/wiki/Polo_Grounds" title="Polo Grounds">
       Polo Grounds
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/155th_Street_(Manhattan)" title="155th Street (Manhattan)">
       155th Street
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Eighth_Avenue_(Manhattan)" title="Eighth Avenue (Manhattan)">
       Eighth Avenue
      </a>
      from their inception in 1883—except for 1889, when they split their time between
      <a href="/wiki/Jersey_City,_New_Jersey" title="Jersey City, New Jersey">
       Jersey City
      </a>
      and Staten Island, and when they played in Hilltop Park in 1911—until they headed west with the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Dodgers" title="Brooklyn Dodgers">
       Brooklyn Dodgers
      </a>
      after the 1957 season.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245">
       <a href="#cite_note-245">
        [241]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The New York Yankees began their franchise as the Highlanders, named for
      <a href="/wiki/Hilltop_Park" title="Hilltop Park">
       Hilltop Park
      </a>
      , where they played from their creation in 1903 until 1912. The team moved to the Polo Grounds with the 1913 season, where they were officially christened the
      <i>
       New York Yankees
      </i>
      , remaining there until they moved across the
      <a href="/wiki/Harlem_River" title="Harlem River">
       Harlem River
      </a>
      in 1923 to
      <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium_(1923)" title="Yankee Stadium (1923)">
       Yankee Stadium
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246">
       <a href="#cite_note-246">
        [242]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">
       New York Mets
      </a>
      played in the Polo Grounds in 1962 and 1963, their first two seasons, before
      <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">
       Shea Stadium
      </a>
      was completed in 1964.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247">
       <a href="#cite_note-247">
        [243]
       </a>
      </sup>
      After the Mets departed, the Polo Grounds was demolished in April 1964, replaced by public housing.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248">
       <a href="#cite_note-248">
        [244]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249">
       <a href="#cite_note-249">
        [245]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The first national college-level basketball championship, the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Invitation_Tournament" title="National Invitation Tournament">
       National Invitation Tournament
      </a>
      , was held in New York in 1938 and remains in the city.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250">
       <a href="#cite_note-250">
        [246]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Knicks" title="New York Knicks">
       New York Knicks
      </a>
      started play in 1946 as one of the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">
       National Basketball Association
      </a>
      's original teams, playing their first home games at the
      <a href="/wiki/69th_Regiment_Armory" title="69th Regiment Armory">
       69th Regiment Armory
      </a>
      , before making Madison Square Garden their permanent home.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251">
       <a href="#cite_note-251">
        [247]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Liberty" title="New York Liberty">
       New York Liberty
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_National_Basketball_Association" title="Women's National Basketball Association">
       WNBA
      </a>
      have shared the Garden with the Knicks since their creation in 1997 as one of the league's original eight teams.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252">
       <a href="#cite_note-252">
        [248]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Rucker_Park" title="Rucker Park">
       Rucker Park
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Harlem" title="Harlem">
       Harlem
      </a>
      is a playground court, famed for its
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Streetball" title="Streetball">
        streetball
       </a>
      </i>
      style of play, where many NBA athletes have played in the summer league.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253">
       <a href="#cite_note-253">
        [249]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Though both of New York City's football teams play today across the
      <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">
       Hudson River
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/MetLife_Stadium" title="MetLife Stadium">
       MetLife Stadium
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/East_Rutherford,_New_Jersey" title="East Rutherford, New Jersey">
       East Rutherford, New Jersey
      </a>
      , both teams started out playing in the Polo Grounds. The
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">
       New York Giants
      </a>
      played side-by-side with their baseball namesakes from the time they entered the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">
       National Football League
      </a>
      in 1925, until crossing over to Yankee Stadium in 1956.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254">
       <a href="#cite_note-254">
        [250]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">
       New York Jets
      </a>
      , originally known as the
      <i>
       Titans
      </i>
      , started out in 1960 at the Polo Grounds, staying there for four seasons before joining the Mets in Queens in 1964.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255">
       <a href="#cite_note-255">
        [251]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Rangers" title="New York Rangers">
       New York Rangers
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">
       National Hockey League
      </a>
      have played in the various locations of Madison Square Garden since their founding in the 1926–1927 season. The Rangers were predated by the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Americans" title="New York Americans">
       New York Americans
      </a>
      , who started play in the Garden the previous season, lasting until the team folded after the 1941–1942 NHL season, a season it played in the Garden as the
      <i>
       Brooklyn Americans
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256">
       <a href="#cite_note-256">
        [252]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Cosmos_(1971%E2%80%931985)" title="New York Cosmos (1971–1985)">
       New York Cosmos
      </a>
      of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_American_Soccer_League_(1968%E2%80%931984)" title="North American Soccer League (1968–1984)">
       North American Soccer League
      </a>
      played their home games at
      <a href="/wiki/Downing_Stadium" title="Downing Stadium">
       Downing Stadium
      </a>
      for two seasons, starting in 1974. In 1975, the team signed
      <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="Pelé">
       Pelé
      </a>
      , officially recorded by
      <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">
       FIFA
      </a>
      as the world's greatest soccer player, to a $4.5 million contract, drawing a capacity crowd of 22,500 to watch him lead the team to a 2–0 victory.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257">
       <a href="#cite_note-257">
        [253]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The playing pitch and facilities at Downing Stadium were in dreadful condition though and as the team's popularity grew they too left for Yankee Stadium, and then Giants Stadium. The stadium was demolished in 2002 to make way for the $45 million, 4,754-seat
      <a href="/wiki/Icahn_Stadium" title="Icahn Stadium">
       Icahn Stadium
      </a>
      , which includes an Olympic-standard 400-meter running track and, as part of Pele's and the Cosmos' legacy, includes a
      <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">
       FIFA
      </a>
      -approved floodlit soccer stadium that hosts matches between the 48 youth teams of a Manhattan soccer club.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258">
       <a href="#cite_note-258">
        [254]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259">
       <a href="#cite_note-259">
        [255]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">
       Government
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Government">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Government_of_New_York_City" title="Government of New York City">
       Government of New York City
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Municipal_Building_-_New_York_City.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" height="333" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Municipal_Building_-_New_York_City.jpg/250px-Municipal_Building_-_New_York_City.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Municipal_Building_-_New_York_City.jpg/375px-Municipal_Building_-_New_York_City.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Municipal_Building_-_New_York_City.jpg/500px-Municipal_Building_-_New_York_City.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Municipal_Building_-_New_York_City.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Municipal_Building" title="Manhattan Municipal Building">
         Manhattan Municipal Building
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Since New York City's consolidation in 1898, Manhattan has been governed by the New York City Charter, which has provided for a strong
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayor-council_government" title="Mayor-council government">
       mayor-council system
      </a>
      since its revision in 1989.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260">
       <a href="#cite_note-260">
        [256]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The centralized New York City government is responsible for public education, correctional institutions, libraries, public safety, recreational facilities, sanitation, water supply, and welfare services in Manhattan.
     </p>
     <p>
      The office of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Borough_President" title="Borough President">
       Borough President
      </a>
      was created in the consolidation of 1898 to balance centralization with local authority. Each borough president had a powerful administrative role derived from having a vote on the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Board_of_Estimate" title="New York City Board of Estimate">
       New York City Board of Estimate
      </a>
      , which was responsible for creating and approving the city's budget and proposals for land use. In 1989, the
      <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">
       Supreme Court of the United States
      </a>
      declared the Board of Estimate unconstitutional because Brooklyn, the most populous borough, had no greater effective representation on the Board than Staten Island, the least populous borough, a violation of the
      <a href="/wiki/Fourteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">
       Fourteenth Amendment's
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Equal_Protection_Clause" title="Equal Protection Clause">
       Equal Protection Clause
      </a>
      pursuant to the high court's 1964 "one man, one vote" decision.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261">
       <a href="#cite_note-261">
        [257]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Since 1990, the largely powerless Borough President has acted as an advocate for the borough at the mayoral agencies, the City Council, the New York state government, and corporations. Manhattan's current
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Borough_President" title="Borough President">
       Borough President
      </a>
      is
      <a href="/wiki/Gale_Brewer" title="Gale Brewer">
       Gale Brewer
      </a>
      , elected as a
      <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">
       Democrat
      </a>
      in November 2013 with 82.9% of the vote.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262">
       <a href="#cite_note-262">
        [258]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Brewer replaced
      <a href="/wiki/Scott_Stringer" title="Scott Stringer">
       Scott Stringer
      </a>
      , who went on to become New York City Comptroller.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyrus_Vance,_Jr." title="Cyrus Vance, Jr.">
       Cyrus Vance
      </a>
      , a Democrat, has been the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_County_District_Attorney" title="New York County District Attorney">
       District Attorney of New York County
      </a>
      since 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263">
       <a href="#cite_note-263">
        [259]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Manhattan has ten City Council members, the third largest contingent among the five boroughs. It also has twelve administrative districts, each served by a local Community Board. Community Boards are representative bodies that field complaints and serve as advocates for local residents. As the host of the UN, the borough is home to the world's largest international
      <a href="/wiki/Consul_(representative)" title="Consul (representative)">
       consular corps
      </a>
      , comprising 105 consulates, consulates general and honorary consulates.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264">
       <a href="#cite_note-264">
        [260]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is also the home of
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Hall" title="New York City Hall">
       New York City Hall
      </a>
      , the seat of New York City government housing the
      <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_New_York_City" title="Mayor of New York City">
       Mayor of New York City
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Council" title="New York City Council">
       New York City Council
      </a>
      . The mayor's staff and thirteen municipal agencies are located in the nearby
      <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Municipal_Building" title="Manhattan Municipal Building">
       Manhattan Municipal Building
      </a>
      , completed in 1916, one of the largest governmental buildings in the world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265">
       <a href="#cite_note-265">
        [261]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin:0em; font-size:90%;">

      <tr>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
       Politics
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Politics">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Community_Boards_of_Manhattan" title="Community Boards of Manhattan">
       Community Boards of Manhattan
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">
       Democratic Party
      </a>
      holds most public offices. Registered
      <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">
       Republicans
      </a>
      are a minority in the borough, constituting 9.88% of the electorate as of April 2016. Registered Republicans are more than 20% of the electorate only in the neighborhoods of the
      <a href="/wiki/Upper_East_Side" title="Upper East Side">
       Upper East Side
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Financial_District,_Manhattan" title="Financial District, Manhattan">
       Financial District
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
         <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2016)">
          when?
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      The Democrats account for 68.41% of those registered to vote, while 17.94% of voters are unaffiliated.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267">
       <a href="#cite_note-267">
        [263]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268">
       <a href="#cite_note-268">
        [264]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Manhattan is divided between three congressional districts, all of which are represented by Democrats.
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Jerrold_Nadler" title="Jerrold Nadler">
        Jerrold Nadler
       </a>
       represents the
       <a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_10th_congressional_district" title="New York's 10th congressional district">
        10th district
       </a>
       , based on the West Side, which covers most of the Upper West Side,
       <a href="/wiki/Hell%27s_Kitchen,_Manhattan" title="Hell's Kitchen, Manhattan">
        Hell's Kitchen
       </a>
       , Chelsea, Greenwich Village,
       <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Manhattan" title="Chinatown, Manhattan">
        Chinatown
       </a>
       , Tribeca and Battery Park City, as well as some sections of Southwest Brooklyn.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carolyn_B._Maloney" title="Carolyn B. Maloney">
        Carolyn B. Maloney
       </a>
       represents the
       <a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_12th_congressional_district" title="New York's 12th congressional district">
        12th district
       </a>
       , the so-called "Silk Stocking" district that was the political base for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teddy_Roosevelt" title="Teddy Roosevelt">
        Teddy Roosevelt
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/John_Lindsay" title="John Lindsay">
        John Lindsay
       </a>
       . It covers most of the
       <a href="/wiki/Upper_East_Side" title="Upper East Side">
        Upper East Side
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Yorkville,_Manhattan" title="Yorkville, Manhattan">
        Yorkville
       </a>
       , Gramercy Park, Roosevelt Island and most of the
       <a href="/wiki/Lower_East_Side" title="Lower East Side">
        Lower East Side
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/East_Village,_Manhattan" title="East Village, Manhattan">
        East Village
       </a>
       , as well as portions of western Queens.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Nydia_Vel%C3%A1zquez" title="Nydia Velázquez">
        Nydia Velázquez
       </a>
       of the Brooklyn/Queens-based
       <a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_7th_congressional_district" title="New York's 7th congressional district">
        7th district
       </a>
       , represents a few heavily Puerto Rican sections of the
       <a href="/wiki/Lower_East_Side" title="Lower East Side">
        Lower East Side
       </a>
       , including Avenues C and D of
       <a href="/wiki/Alphabet_City,_Manhattan" title="Alphabet City, Manhattan">
        Alphabet City
       </a>
       .
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      No
      <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">
       Republican
      </a>
      has won the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election" title="United States presidential election">
       presidential election
      </a>
      in Manhattan since
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1924" title="United States presidential election, 1924">
       1924
      </a>
      , when
      <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Coolidge" title="Calvin Coolidge">
       Calvin Coolidge
      </a>
      won a plurality of the New York County vote over Democrat
      <a href="/wiki/John_W._Davis" title="John W. Davis">
       John W. Davis
      </a>
      , 41.20%–39.55%.
      <a href="/wiki/Warren_G._Harding" title="Warren G. Harding">
       Warren G. Harding
      </a>
      was the most recent Republican presidential candidate to win a majority of the Manhattan vote, with 59.22% of the 1920 vote.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269">
       <a href="#cite_note-269">
        [265]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the 2004 presidential election, Democrat
      <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">
       John Kerry
      </a>
      received 82.1% of the vote in Manhattan and Republican
      <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">
       George W. Bush
      </a>
      received 16.7%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270">
       <a href="#cite_note-270">
        [266]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The borough is the most important source of funding for presidential campaigns in the United States; in 2004, it was home to six of the top seven
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ZIP_code" title="ZIP code">
       ZIP codes
      </a>
      in the nation for political contributions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271">
       <a href="#cite_note-271">
        [267]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The top ZIP code, 10021 on the Upper East Side, generated the most money for the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election" title="United States presidential election">
       United States presidential election
      </a>
      for all presidential candidates, including both Kerry and Bush during the 2004 election.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272">
       <a href="#cite_note-272">
        [268]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Farley_PO_jeh.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2305" data-file-width="3072" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Farley_PO_jeh.JPG/250px-Farley_PO_jeh.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Farley_PO_jeh.JPG/375px-Farley_PO_jeh.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Farley_PO_jeh.JPG/500px-Farley_PO_jeh.JPG 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Farley_PO_jeh.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Farley_Post_Office" title="James Farley Post Office">
         James Farley Post Office
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_offices">
       Federal offices
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Federal offices">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The United States Postal Service operates post offices in Manhattan. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Farley_Post_Office" title="James Farley Post Office">
       James Farley Post Office
      </a>
      in Midtown Manhattan is New York City's main post office.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273">
       <a href="#cite_note-273">
        [269]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is located at 421
      <a href="/wiki/Eighth_Avenue_(Manhattan)" title="Eighth Avenue (Manhattan)">
       Eighth Avenue
      </a>
      , between
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/31st_Street_(Manhattan)" title="31st Street (Manhattan)">
       31st Street
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/33rd_Street_(Manhattan)" title="33rd Street (Manhattan)">
       33rd Street
      </a>
      . The post office stopped 24-hour service on May 9, 2009, due to decreasing mail traffic.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274">
       <a href="#cite_note-274">
        [270]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Both the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Southern_District_of_New_York" title="United States District Court for the Southern District of New York">
       United States District Court for the Southern District of New York
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Second_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Second Circuit">
       United States Court of Appeals for the Second Circuit
      </a>
      are located in lower Manhattan's
      <a href="/wiki/Foley_Square" title="Foley Square">
       Foley Square
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Attorney_for_the_Southern_District_of_New_York" title="United States Attorney for the Southern District of New York">
       U.S. Attorney
      </a>
      and other federal offices and agencies maintain locations in that area.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Crime_and_public_safety">
       Crime and public safety
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Crime and public safety">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_New_York_City" title="Crime in New York City">
       Crime in New York City
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NYPD_boat99pct.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1896" data-file-width="2552" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/NYPD_boat99pct.jpg/225px-NYPD_boat99pct.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/NYPD_boat99pct.jpg/338px-NYPD_boat99pct.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/NYPD_boat99pct.jpg/450px-NYPD_boat99pct.jpg 2x" width="225"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NYPD_boat99pct.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        An
        <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Police_Department" title="New York City Police Department">
         NYPD
        </a>
        boat patrols
        <a href="/wiki/New_York_Harbor" title="New York Harbor">
         New York Harbor
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leslie_five_points_new_york_1885_3c22660v.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2985" data-file-width="3736" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Leslie_five_points_new_york_1885_3c22660v.jpg/250px-Leslie_five_points_new_york_1885_3c22660v.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Leslie_five_points_new_york_1885_3c22660v.jpg/375px-Leslie_five_points_new_york_1885_3c22660v.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Leslie_five_points_new_york_1885_3c22660v.jpg/500px-Leslie_five_points_new_york_1885_3c22660v.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leslie_five_points_new_york_1885_3c22660v.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A slum tour through the
        <a href="/wiki/Five_Points,_Manhattan" title="Five Points, Manhattan">
         Five Points
        </a>
        in an 1885 sketch
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Starting in the mid-19th century, the United States became a magnet for immigrants seeking to escape poverty in their home countries. After arriving in New York, many new arrivals ended up living in squalor in the
      <a href="/wiki/Slum" title="Slum">
       slums
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Five_Points,_Manhattan" title="Five Points, Manhattan">
       Five Points
      </a>
      neighborhood, an area between
      <a href="/wiki/Broadway_(Manhattan)" title="Broadway (Manhattan)">
       Broadway
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Bowery" title="Bowery">
       Bowery
      </a>
      , northeast of
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Hall" title="New York City Hall">
       New York City Hall
      </a>
      . By the 1820s, the area was home to many gambling dens and
      <a href="/wiki/Brothel" title="Brothel">
       brothels
      </a>
      , and was known as a dangerous place to go. In 1842,
      <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">
       Charles Dickens
      </a>
      visited the area and was appalled at the horrendous living conditions he had seen.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275">
       <a href="#cite_note-275">
        [271]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The area was so notorious that it even caught the attention of
      <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">
       Abraham Lincoln
      </a>
      , who visited the area before his
      <a href="/wiki/Cooper_Union_speech" title="Cooper Union speech">
       Cooper Union speech
      </a>
      in 1860.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276">
       <a href="#cite_note-276">
        [272]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The predominantly Irish
      <a href="/wiki/Five_Points_Gang" title="Five Points Gang">
       Five Points Gang
      </a>
      was one of the country's first major
      <a href="/wiki/Organized_crime" title="Organized crime">
       organized crime
      </a>
      entities.
     </p>
     <p>
      As Italian immigration grew in the early 20th century many joined ethnic gangs, including
      <a href="/wiki/Al_Capone" title="Al Capone">
       Al Capone
      </a>
      , who got his start in crime with the
      <a href="/wiki/Five_Points_Gang" title="Five Points Gang">
       Five Points Gang
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277">
       <a href="#cite_note-277">
        [273]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Mafia" title="Mafia">
       Mafia
      </a>
      (also known as
      <i>
       Cosa Nostra
      </i>
      ) first developed in the mid-19th century in
      <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">
       Sicily
      </a>
      and spread to the
      <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">
       East Coast of the United States
      </a>
      during the late 19th century following waves of Sicilian and Southern Italian emigration.
      <a href="/wiki/Lucky_Luciano" title="Lucky Luciano">
       Lucky Luciano
      </a>
      established Cosa Nostra in Manhattan, forming alliances with other criminal enterprises, including the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_mob" title="Jewish mob">
       Jewish mob
      </a>
      , led by
      <a href="/wiki/Meyer_Lansky" title="Meyer Lansky">
       Meyer Lansky
      </a>
      , the leading Jewish gangster of that period.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smithsonian_278-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Smithsonian-278">
        [274]
       </a>
      </sup>
      From 1920–1933,
      <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_in_the_United_States" title="Prohibition in the United States">
       Prohibition
      </a>
      helped create a thriving
      <a href="/wiki/Black_market" title="Black market">
       black market
      </a>
      in liquor, upon which the Mafia was quick to capitalize.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smithsonian_278-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Smithsonian-278">
        [274]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As in the whole of New York City, Manhattan experienced a sharp increase in crime during the 1960s and 1970s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279">
       <a href="#cite_note-279">
        [275]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Since 1990, crime in Manhattan has plummeted in all categories tracked by the CompStat profile. A borough that saw 503 murders in 1990 has seen a drop of nearly 88% to 62 in 2008. Robbery and burglary are down by more than 80% during the period, and auto theft has been reduced by more than 93%. In the seven major crime categories tracked by the system, overall crime has declined by more than 75% since 1990, and year-to-date statistics through May 2009 show continuing declines.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280">
       <a href="#cite_note-280">
        [276]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Based on 2005 data, New York City has the lowest crime rate among the ten largest cities in the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_281-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-281">
        [277]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">
       Housing
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Housing">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:17-23_West_16th_St.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1705" data-file-width="2268" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/17-23_West_16th_St.jpg/250px-17-23_West_16th_St.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/17-23_West_16th_St.jpg/375px-17-23_West_16th_St.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/17-23_West_16th_St.jpg/500px-17-23_West_16th_St.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:17-23_West_16th_St.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Row of townhouses on 17–23 West 16th Street
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tribeca_hudson_st.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Tribeca_hudson_st.jpg/250px-Tribeca_hudson_st.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Tribeca_hudson_st.jpg/375px-Tribeca_hudson_st.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Tribeca_hudson_st.jpg/500px-Tribeca_hudson_st.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tribeca_hudson_st.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Loft buildings (now apartments) in
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TriBeCa" title="TriBeCa">
         TriBeCa
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      During Manhattan's early history, wood construction and poor access to water supplies left the city vulnerable to fires. In 1776, shortly after the
      <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">
       Continental Army
      </a>
      evacuated Manhattan and left it to the British, a massive fire broke out destroying one-third of the city and some 500 houses.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282">
       <a href="#cite_note-282">
        [278]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The rise of immigration near the turn of the 20th century left major portions of Manhattan, especially the
      <a href="/wiki/Lower_East_Side" title="Lower East Side">
       Lower East Side
      </a>
      , densely packed with recent arrivals, crammed into unhealthy and unsanitary housing.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tenements" title="Tenements">
       Tenements
      </a>
      were usually five-stories high, constructed on the then-typical 25x100 lots, with "cockroach landlords" exploiting the new immigrants.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283">
       <a href="#cite_note-283">
        [279]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTTenements_284-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYTTenements-284">
        [280]
       </a>
      </sup>
      By 1929, stricter fire codes and the increased use of elevators in residential buildings, were the impetus behind a new housing code that effectively ended the tenement as a form of new construction, though many tenement buildings survive today on the East Side of the borough.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTTenements_284-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYTTenements-284">
        [280]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Manhattan offers a wide array of public and private housing options. There were 852,575 housing units in 2013
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ManhattanQuickFacts_1-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-ManhattanQuickFacts-1">
        [1]
       </a>
      </sup>
      at an average density of 37,345 per square mile (14,419/km²). As of 2003
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , only 20.3% of Manhattan residents lived in owner-occupied housing, the second-lowest rate of all counties in the nation, behind the Bronx.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OwnerOccupied_285-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-OwnerOccupied-285">
        [281]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Although the city of New York has the highest average cost for rent in the United States, it simultaneously hosts a higher average of income per capita. Because of this, rent is a lower percentage of annual income than in several other American cities.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-name_286-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-name-286">
        [282]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of 2012
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , Manhattan's real estate market for luxury housing was among the most expensive in the world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287">
       <a href="#cite_note-287">
        [283]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">
       Infrastructure
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
       Transportation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Transportation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_New_York_City" title="Transportation in New York City">
       Transportation in New York City
      </a>
     </div>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transportation">
       Public transportation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Public transportation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Central_Station_Main_Concourse_Jan_2006.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1287" data-file-width="2305" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Grand_Central_Station_Main_Concourse_Jan_2006.jpg/250px-Grand_Central_Station_Main_Concourse_Jan_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Grand_Central_Station_Main_Concourse_Jan_2006.jpg/375px-Grand_Central_Station_Main_Concourse_Jan_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Grand_Central_Station_Main_Concourse_Jan_2006.jpg/500px-Grand_Central_Station_Main_Concourse_Jan_2006.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Central_Station_Main_Concourse_Jan_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Grand_Central_Terminal" title="Grand Central Terminal">
         Grand Central Terminal
        </a>
        is a
        <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">
         National Historic Landmark
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Staten_Island_Ferry-Battery_Park-2012.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Staten_Island_Ferry-Battery_Park-2012.jpg/250px-Staten_Island_Ferry-Battery_Park-2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Staten_Island_Ferry-Battery_Park-2012.jpg/375px-Staten_Island_Ferry-Battery_Park-2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Staten_Island_Ferry-Battery_Park-2012.jpg/500px-Staten_Island_Ferry-Battery_Park-2012.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Staten_Island_Ferry-Battery_Park-2012.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island_Ferry" title="Staten Island Ferry">
         Staten Island Ferry
        </a>
        , seen from
        <a href="/wiki/Battery_Park" title="Battery Park">
         Battery Park
        </a>
        crosses
        <a href="/wiki/Upper_New_York_Bay" title="Upper New York Bay">
         Upper New York Bay
        </a>
        providing free public transportation between
        <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island" title="Staten Island">
         Staten Island
        </a>
        and Manhattan.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_transportation_in_New_York_City" title="Public transportation in New York City">
       Public transportation in New York City
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Manhattan is unique in the U.S. for intense use of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_transportation" title="Public transportation">
       public transportation
      </a>
      and lack of private car ownership. While 88% of Americans nationwide drive to their jobs, with only 5% using public transport, mass transit is the dominant form of travel for residents of Manhattan, with 72% of borough residents using public transport to get to work, while only 18% drove.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2001summary_288-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-2001summary-288">
        [284]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289">
       <a href="#cite_note-289">
        [285]
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to the 2000 United States Census, 77.5% of Manhattan households do not own a car.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290">
       <a href="#cite_note-290">
        [286]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2008, Mayor Bloomberg
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_congestion_pricing" title="New York congestion pricing">
       proposed
      </a>
      a
      <a href="/wiki/Congestion_pricing" title="Congestion pricing">
       congestion pricing
      </a>
      system to regulate entering Manhattan south of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/60th_Street_(Manhattan)" title="60th Street (Manhattan)">
       60th Street
      </a>
      . The state legislature rejected the proposal in June 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291">
       <a href="#cite_note-291">
        [287]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">
       New York City Subway
      </a>
      , the largest
      <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">
       subway
      </a>
      system in the world by number of stations, is the primary means of travel within the city, linking every borough except Staten Island. There are
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_New_York_City_Subway_stations_in_Manhattan" title="List of New York City Subway stations in Manhattan">
       148 subway stations in Manhattan and four under construction
      </a>
      , out of the 469 stations. A second subway, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_Authority_Trans-Hudson" title="Port Authority Trans-Hudson">
       Port Authority Trans-Hudson
      </a>
      (PATH) system, connects
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_PATH_stations" title="List of PATH stations">
       six stations in Manhattan
      </a>
      to northern
      <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">
       New Jersey
      </a>
      . Passengers pay fares with pay-per-ride
      <a href="/wiki/MetroCard_(New_York_City)" title="MetroCard (New York City)">
       MetroCards
      </a>
      , which are valid on all city buses and subways, as well as on PATH trains.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292">
       <a href="#cite_note-292">
        [288]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293">
       <a href="#cite_note-293">
        [289]
       </a>
      </sup>
      There are 7-day and 30-day MetroCards that allow unlimited trips on all subways (except PATH) and MTA bus routes (except for express buses).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294">
       <a href="#cite_note-294">
        [290]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The PATH QuickCard is being phased out, having been replaced by the
      <a href="/wiki/SmartLink_(smart_card)" title="SmartLink (smart card)">
       SmartLink
      </a>
      . The MTA is testing "smart card" payment systems to replace the MetroCard.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295">
       <a href="#cite_note-295">
        [291]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Regional_rail" title="Regional rail">
       Commuter rail
      </a>
      services operating to and from Manhattan are the
      <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Rail_Road" title="Long Island Rail Road">
       Long Island Rail Road
      </a>
      (which connects Manhattan and other New York City boroughs to
      <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">
       Long Island
      </a>
      ), the
      <a href="/wiki/Metro-North_Railroad" title="Metro-North Railroad">
       Metro-North Railroad
      </a>
      (which connects Manhattan to Upstate New York and Southwestern Connecticut) and
      <a href="/wiki/NJ_Transit" title="NJ Transit">
       NJ Transit
      </a>
      trains to various points in New Jersey. Multibillion-dollar heavy-rail transit projects under construction in Manhattan include the
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Avenue_Subway" title="Second Avenue Subway">
       Second Avenue Subway
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/East_Side_Access" title="East Side Access">
       East Side Access
      </a>
      project, and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_Transportation_Hub" title="World Trade Center Transportation Hub">
       World Trade Center Transportation Hub
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296">
       <a href="#cite_note-296">
        [292]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Two multi-billion-dollar projects were completed in the mid-2010s, with the $1.4 billion
      <a href="/wiki/Fulton_Center" title="Fulton Center">
       Fulton Center
      </a>
      having been completed in November 2014
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297">
       <a href="#cite_note-297">
        [293]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the $2.4 billion
      <a href="/wiki/7_Subway_Extension" title="7 Subway Extension">
       7 Subway Extension
      </a>
      having been completed in September 2015.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298">
       <a href="#cite_note-298">
        [294]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Transit_Authority" title="New York City Transit Authority">
       MTA New York City Transit
      </a>
      offers a wide variety of local buses within Manhattan under the brand
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_City_Bus" title="New York City Bus">
       New York City Bus
      </a>
      . An extensive network of express bus routes serves commuters and other travelers heading into Manhattan. The bus system served 784 million passengers citywide in 2011, placing the bus system's ridership as the highest in the nation, and more than double the ridership of the second-place Los Angeles system.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299">
       <a href="#cite_note-299">
        [295]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Island_Tramway" title="Roosevelt Island Tramway">
       Roosevelt Island Tramway
      </a>
      , one of two commuter cable car systems in North America, whisks commuters between
      <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Island" title="Roosevelt Island">
       Roosevelt Island
      </a>
      and Manhattan in less than five minutes, and has been serving the island since 1978. (The other system in North America is the
      <a href="/wiki/Portland_Aerial_Tram" title="Portland Aerial Tram">
       Portland Aerial Tram
      </a>
      .)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300">
       <a href="#cite_note-300">
        [296]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301">
       <a href="#cite_note-301">
        [297]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Staten_Island_Ferry" title="Staten Island Ferry">
       Staten Island Ferry
      </a>
      , which runs 24 hours a day, 365 days a year, annually carries over 21 million passengers on the 5.2-mile (8.4 km) run between Manhattan and Staten Island. Each weekday, five vessels transport about 65,000 passengers on 109 boat trips.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302">
       <a href="#cite_note-302">
        [298]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303">
       <a href="#cite_note-303">
        [299]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The ferry has been fare-free since 1997, when the then-50-cent fare was eliminated.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304">
       <a href="#cite_note-304">
        [300]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The metro region's commuter rail lines converge at
      <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Station_(New_York_City)" title="Pennsylvania Station (New York City)">
       Penn Station
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Grand_Central_Terminal" title="Grand Central Terminal">
       Grand Central Terminal
      </a>
      , on the west and east sides of Midtown Manhattan, respectively. They are the two busiest rail stations in the United States. About one-third of users of mass transit and two-thirds of railway passengers in the country live in New York and its suburbs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305">
       <a href="#cite_note-305">
        [301]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">
       Amtrak
      </a>
      provides inter-city passenger rail service from Penn Station to
      <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">
       Boston
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">
       Philadelphia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">
       Baltimore
      </a>
      , and Washington, D.C.;
      <a href="/wiki/Upstate_New_York" title="Upstate New York">
       Upstate New York
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">
       New England
      </a>
      ; cross-Canadian border service to
      <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">
       Toronto
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">
       Montreal
      </a>
      ; and destinations in the
      <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">
       Southern
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">
       Midwestern United States
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Taxis">
       Taxis
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Taxis">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Taxicabs_of_New_York_City" title="Taxicabs of New York City">
       Taxicabs of New York City
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      New York's iconic yellow
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taxicabs" title="Taxicabs">
       taxicabs
      </a>
      , which number 13,087 city-wide and must have the requisite medallion authorizing the pick up of street hails, are ubiquitous in the borough.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306">
       <a href="#cite_note-306">
        [302]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Various private
      <a href="/wiki/Transportation_network_company" title="Transportation network company">
       transportation network companies
      </a>
      compete in Manhattan with each other and with the city's taxicabs.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Bikes">
       Bikes
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Bikes">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Cycling_in_New_York_City" title="Cycling in New York City">
       Cycling in New York City
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Manhattan also has tens of thousands of
      <a href="/wiki/Cycling_in_New_York_City" title="Cycling in New York City">
       bicycle commuters
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Streets_and_roads">
       <span id="Streets">
       </span>
       <span id="Roads_and_Streets">
       </span>
       Streets and roads
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manhattan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Streets and roads">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LOC_Brooklyn_Bridge_and_East_River_2_cropped.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3422" data-file-width="4332" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/LOC_Brooklyn_Bridge_and_East_River_2_cropped.jpg/250px-LOC_Brooklyn_Bridge_and_East_River_2_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/LOC_Brooklyn_Bridge_and_East_River_2_cropped.jpg/375px-LOC_Brooklyn_Bridge_and_East_River_2_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/LOC_Brooklyn_Bridge_and_East_River_2_cropped.jpg/500px-LOC_Brooklyn_Bridge_and_East_River_2_cropped.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LOC_Brooklyn_Bridge_and_East_River_2_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Bridge" title="Brooklyn Bridge">
